# Prior: Rex Session 65 shipped US-199 — Spool Data v2 Story 1 (6 new Mode 01 PIDs + ELM_VOLTAGE adapter command) end-to-end on sprint/pi-harden. New `src/pi/obdii/decoders.py` (DecodedReading dataclass + 7 decoder fns + ParameterDecoderEntry + PARAMETER_DECODERS registry) maps Spool-facing parameter_names → (python-obd command, PID code, decoder fn): FUEL_SYSTEM_STATUS→FUEL_STATUS/0x03 (enum→code+textLabel), MIL_ON→STATUS/0x01 (bool→1.0/0.0+ON/OFF), DTC_COUNT→STATUS/0x01 (int→float), O2_BANK1_SENSOR2_V→O2_B1S2/0x15 (tuple-first-field voltage), RUNTIME_SEC→RUN_TIME/0x1F (uint16 seconds), BATTERY_V→ELM_VOLTAGE/None (adapter-level ATRV — NOT PID 0x42 which Session 23 confirmed unsupported on 2G), BAROMETRIC_KPA→BAROMETRIC_PRESSURE/0x33 (uint8 kPa). New `src/pi/obdii/pid_probe.py` (SupportedPidSet + probeSupportedPids) reads python-obd auto-probed `supported_commands` at connection-open, normalizes to lowercase two-hex-char PID keys (normalizes on dataclass __post_init__ so direct constructor calls also work), filters to Mode 01 only (Mode 03/09 skipped since bitmap only covers Mode 01), falls back to SupportedPidSet.alwaysSupported() on probe-unavailable — null-response silent-skip remains the downstream safety net. ObdConnection.connect() post-success calls `_runSupportedPidProbe()` (best-effort; probe failure never fails the connection) and caches result on `self.supportedPids`. ObdDataLogger.queryParameter consults PARAMETER_DECODERS first — for decoder-registered names, `_assertPidSupported` raises `ParameterNotSupportedError` before dispatch for Mode 01 PIDs not in the cache (adapter commands with pidCode=None always bypass the gate), then `_queryViaDecoder` runs the python-obd query under the entry's obdCommand name and wraps the decoder output as a LoggedReading with `reading.unit` carrying the enum textLabel where present. Enum encoding for FUEL_SYSTEM_STATUS: 1=OL, 2=CL, 3=OL-drive, 4=OL-fault, 5=CL-fault, 0=UNKNOWN — numeric code in value (REAL NOT NULL schema invariant), text label in unit (TEXT). config.json: 7 new entries in `pi.realtimeData.parameters` (logData=true) + 6 new entries across `pi.pollingTiers` — FUEL_SYSTEM_STATUS tier1 (1 Hz), MIL_ON/DTC_COUNT/O2_BANK1_SENSOR2_V tier2 (0.3 Hz), RUNTIME_SEC/BATTERY_V tier3 (0.1 Hz), BAROMETRIC_KPA tier4 (0.03 Hz). BATTERY_V uses the literal string "ELM_VOLTAGE" in the tier config's pid field as an adapter-level sentinel; CONTROL_MODULE_VOLTAGE (0x42) kept in tier4 with Session 23 unsupported-caveat for probe-matrix documentation. Theoretical poll rate post-US-199 = 8.27 PIDs/sec at 1 Hz cycle cadence; Session 23 measured 0.36x throttle ratio (11 PIDs at theoretical ~7.0/s yielded 2.5/s measured) means expected actual ~3.0/s — marginally over 2.5/s envelope but well within K-line physical throttling. Documented in specs/obd2-research.md new "Sprint 14 US-199" section. specs/grounded-knowledge.md new "Battery Voltage via ELM_VOLTAGE (2G workaround) — Thresholds" subsection captures Spool Phase 1 battery-voltage spec (normal 13.5-14.5V running, caution 12.5-13.5V/14.5-14.8V, danger <12.0V or >15.0V) at `pi.tieredThresholds.batteryVoltage` config path — PM Rule 7 source-of-truth. TDD: 82 new tests RED-first (ImportError on pid_probe + decoders, then AssertionError on empty PARAMETER_DECODERS) before any src/ edit, then GREEN after implementation. tests/pi/obdii/test_pid_probe.py = 18 tests (SupportedPidSet core API + normalize-on-construct + probe happy path over python-obd supported_commands shape + probe skips non-Mode-01 + probe falls back on disconnect/None/missing-attr + parameterized hex normalization). tests/pi/obdii/test_decoders_v2.py = 35 tests (decodeFuelSystemStatus parametrized over 5 canonical python-obd status strings + UNKNOWN + bare-string acceptance, decodeMilStatus MIL=True/False + dict-style fallback, decodeDtcCount parametrized 0/1/5/42/127 + malformed status→zero, decodeRuntimeSec 0/42/65535-rollover, decodeBarometricKpa nominal + Chicago-sea-level, decodeBatteryVoltage 12.8V + range 11.5/12.0/13.8/14.5, decodeO2PostCatVoltage tuple-first-field + bare-numeric fallback, PARAMETER_DECODERS registry invariants for all 7 names). tests/pi/obdii/test_poll_set_expansion.py = 18 tests (all 6 new PIDs present in loaded pollingConfig with correct hex codes, BATTERY_V must NOT bind to 0x42, existing 11 PIDs unchanged per scope.doNotTouch, Spool-spec tier assignments parametrized 7-way, theoretical aggregate rate ≤10.0/s documented-ceiling assertion). tests/pi/obdii/test_logger_v2_decoders.py = 11 integration tests (FUEL_SYSTEM_STATUS round-trip via mocked python-obd with value+textLabel assertions, BATTERY_V routes to ELM_VOLTAGE command + bypasses SupportedPidSet gate, MIL_ON/DTC_COUNT extract from STATUS response, supportedPids explicit-exclude raises ParameterNotSupportedError before dispatch, supportedPids explicit-include proceeds, None-cache treats as supported BC, alwaysSupported proceeds, null-response raises ParameterReadError, legacy RPM path unchanged regression guard). tests/test_polling_tiers.py TestOBDConfigIntegration tier1-4 snapshot assertions extended with new PID names + updated docstrings. # Prior: Rex Session 50 shipped US-154 — Manual sync CLI (scripts/sync_now.py).

## Codebase Patterns
- **Process-wide "current context" accessor for fan-out writers — module-level state with lock, lazy import to dodge package cycles**: US-200 adds a `drive_id` column to 4 capture tables whose writers fan out across 5 files (helpers.py, logger.py, detector.py, analysis/engine.py, alert/manager.py). The drive detector owns the state machine that opens/closes drives; writers need to read "what drive are we in right now" at every INSERT. Three bad alternatives: (a) pass drive_id as parameter through every writer's signature -- 10+ sites, expensive refactor. (b) SQLite trigger AFTER INSERT to auto-populate -- elegant but Pi-only (server stays un-triggered), and server-side writers would need a parallel mechanism. (c) singleton/registry object -- requires wiring a ref through every constructor. US-200's pick: module-level state `_currentDriveId: int | None` + threading.Lock + `setCurrentDriveId/getCurrentDriveId/clearCurrentDriveId` public API. DriveDetector._startDrive calls setCurrentDriveId(newId) after nextDriveId(conn); _endDrive calls setCurrentDriveId(None) AFTER post-drive analysis so statistics rows inherit the closing id. Writers call getCurrentDriveId() at INSERT time. Tests use clearCurrentDriveId() in an autouse fixture to isolate. Key circular-import gotcha: obdii/__init__.py imports pi.alert (for shutdown registration); pi.alert.manager importing src.pi.obdii.drive_id at module level creates a cycle that breaks subprocess-based test_verify_database. Fix: lazy-import inside the function (`def _logAlertToDatabase: from src.pi.obdii.drive_id import getCurrentDriveId`). Same pattern applied to pi.analysis.engine. Live at `src/pi/obdii/drive_id.py::{setCurrentDriveId, getCurrentDriveId}` (US-200). Reusable for any "ambient request-scoped" state that fan-outs need to read (correlation_id in tracing, request user_id in multi-tenant DB filters, session_id in realtime_data-style rows).
- **Idempotent schema migration + column-with-index bundled helper -- DON'T register the new indexes in ALL_INDEXES**: US-200 adds drive_id column + IX_<table>_drive_id index to 4 capture tables.  First attempt registered both in `ALL_SCHEMAS` (DDL in fresh CREATE) + `ALL_INDEXES` (standalone CREATE INDEX).  This blew up on legacy databases where the tables exist WITHOUT drive_id (pre-US-200) because initialize() runs the schema loop first, THEN the index loop, THEN the migration.  When the index loop reaches `CREATE INDEX ... ON realtime_data(drive_id)` on a legacy table, SQLite raises "no such column: drive_id".  Fix: bundle the index creation INSIDE the migration helper (`ensureDriveIdColumn` runs both `ALTER TABLE ADD COLUMN` + `CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS` for that table) and REMOVE the drive_id indexes from `ALL_INDEXES`.  Now the order is: schema DDL creates fresh tables WITH both column + (implicit, because ALL_INDEXES no longer has them) no index + migration runs + migration adds column to legacy tables + migration creates index on ALL tables (fresh + legacy both idempotent via `CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS`).  Fresh tables get the index via the migration's always-run index step; legacy tables get column+index in the same call.  Live at `src/pi/obdii/drive_id.py::ensureDriveIdColumn` (US-200). Reusable for any schema migration that adds a column AND an index for that column -- if the index depends on the column existing, couple them so ordering hazards go away.
- **drive_id as row-level grouping key outperforms time-window reconstruction for per-drive analytics**: Pre-US-200 server analytics filtered realtime_data by `(device_id, timestamp BETWEEN drive.start_time AND drive.end_time)` reconstructed from DriveSummary.  This has three hazards: (1) timestamp-boundary rows belong to "neither" drive when drives are back-to-back.  (2) Rows logged during BT disconnect (engine running but connection_log silent) may fall into gap windows.  (3) Pi clock skew + server tz-aware-vs-naive comparison bugs shift rows into wrong drives.  Row-level drive_id sidesteps all three -- the row itself says which drive it belongs to; no reconstruction.  Per-drive queries become `WHERE drive_id = ?` (indexed, one btree seek) instead of `WHERE timestamp BETWEEN ? AND ?` (range scan over 365 days of data).  Pattern: the new `collectReadingsForDrive(session, driveId=, deviceId=)` in `src/server/analytics/basic.py` is the preferred API post-US-200.  Legacy `_collectReadings(session, drive)` (time-window) kept for pre-US-200 DriveSummary rows where realtime_data.drive_id IS NULL.  Live at `src/server/analytics/basic.py::collectReadingsForDrive` (US-200).  Reusable any time a fan-out table grows a "which logical operation produced me" column that can replace a time-range reconstruction.
- **MAC-vs-path resolution in port-accepting constructors — detect first, bind second, release-iff-owned**: python-OBD (and by analogy any pyserial-backed library) `obd.OBD(portstr=...)` expects a Linux device path like `/dev/rfcomm0`, not a Bluetooth MAC. Passing a MAC produces `ENOENT` on `pyserial.Serial.open()`. US-193's pattern: (1) accept both formats at the config layer — `pi.bluetooth.macAddress` can hold either a MAC or a literal path; the value is intentionally polymorphic. (2) Detect at the connection boundary via a regex module (`bluetooth_helper.isMacAddress`, `^[0-9A-Fa-f]{2}(?::[0-9A-Fa-f]{2}){5}$`); everything that doesn't match is passed through unchanged (BC for operators who set `/dev/rfcomm0` directly, or who inject a COM3-style path). (3) For MAC inputs, resolve via an idempotent `bindRfcomm(mac, device, channel)` helper that calls `rfcomm show N` first to check the current bind state — short-circuit if already bound to the same MAC, release-and-rebind if bound to a different MAC, bind fresh if unbound. (4) Track ownership with a `self._boundRfcomm` flag so `disconnect()` only calls `releaseRfcomm` when this instance performed the bind; path-passthrough operators keep lifecycle ownership. (5) All sudo stays in a bash companion (`scripts/connect_obdlink.sh`) or via sudoers NOPASSWD on `/usr/sbin/rfcomm` — never `subprocess.run(['sudo', ...])` from Python. (6) For test-ability, inject the subprocess runner: `def bindRfcomm(..., subprocessRunner=None)`; production default is a thin wrapper around `subprocess.run` with `capture_output=True, text=True, check=False`; tests pass a FakeRunner that records calls and replays canned `CompletedProcess` tuples. Live at `src/pi/obdii/bluetooth_helper.py` + `src/pi/obdii/obd_connection.py::_resolvePort` (US-193). Reusable for any "resolve abstract identifier to concrete device path" boundary — USB-serial VID/PID -> /dev/ttyUSB0, WireGuard peer -> interface name, anything where the user's config value is a symbol that needs to become a path before a third-party library can open it.
- **AST-based source-level linting is comment/docstring-safe; regex over `inspect.getsource` is not**: US-203's `TestNoDatetimeNowInCaptureWriteFunctions` needs to assert that specific capture-write function bodies contain zero naive `datetime.now()` calls. First attempt used a raw regex over `inspect.getsource(func)` — it correctly failed on the pre-fix code, but after the fix it STILL failed because my own explanatory comments in the fix commits contained the literal text `datetime.now()` (e.g. "Previously used naive datetime.now() -- produced local-time strings"). The regex has no syntactic awareness. Fix: use `ast.parse(textwrap.dedent(source))` + `ast.walk` + match only on `ast.Call` nodes whose `func` is an `ast.Attribute` with `.attr == 'now'` whose `value` is an `ast.Name` matching `datetime` (or an Attribute ending in `datetime`) AND whose `args` + `keywords` are both empty. AST sees through comments and string literals -- docstrings become `ast.Constant` nodes, not Call nodes. Also: when the target is an indented class method, `ast.parse` rejects it; `textwrap.dedent` first. Pattern at `tests/pi/data/test_timestamp_format.py::_findNaiveDatetimeNowCalls` (US-203). Reusable for any "no anti-pattern in this specific function body" test (e.g., "no `print(` in production code", "no `time.sleep(` in a test helper", "no bare `except:` in a critical path").
- **Coerce-at-DB-write-boundary for naive datetime -- minimum-touch alternative to upstream dataclass surgery**: When many writer sites feed a few capture tables but the naive-datetime source lives in upstream `__post_init__` methods (AlertEvent, PowerReading, VoltageReading), the tempting fix is to re-architect the dataclasses to be tz-aware. US-203's Invariant #4 explicitly forbade that ("Do NOT make this story a place to re-architect the upstream dataclasses -- minimum-touch routing through the helper is the goal"). Pattern: at each `cursor.execute("INSERT INTO <capture_table> ... VALUES (?, ...)", (<timestamp_value>, ...))` site, replace the caller-supplied `<timestamp_value>` with a direct `utcIsoNow()` call. The dataclasses keep their naive semantics for in-memory use (session stats, event comparisons), but capture rows are canonical. For APIs where the caller passes an explicit timestamp argument (e.g., `logPowerTransition(db, eventType, timestamp, source)`), keep the parameter for API BC and mark it `# noqa: ARG001 -- kept for BC; DB row uses utcIsoNow at write-time`. This preserves the call-site convention while the persistent row gets canonical. The ~ms drift between "caller's event time" and "DB-write time" is below the canonical format's second resolution anyway. Live at `src/pi/power/power_db.py::logPowerTransition` (US-203 pattern; established by US-202 `drive/detector.py:616` precedent). Reusable for any TD-fix that needs to unify a DB-row format without touching upstream producers.
- **Compute-once-per-transaction for multi-row INSERTs sharing a canonical timestamp -- don't call `utcIsoNow()` in a loop**: `StatisticsEngine._storeStatistics` writes N rows (one per parameter) from a single analysis run, and the `getLatestAnalysisResult` query uses `MAX(analysis_date)` then reloads rows `WHERE analysis_date = ?`. If the INSERT loop calls `utcIsoNow()` per row, each row's timestamp differs by a few microseconds -- the MAX-grouping query then returns only ONE parameter's stats instead of the whole run. Fix: compute the canonical string ONCE before the loop (`canonicalAnalysisDate = toCanonicalIso(result.analysisDate)`) and bind every INSERT to the same value. This requires the upstream `result.analysisDate` to be tz-aware (toCanonicalIso rejects naive); US-203 flipped `analysisDate = datetime.now()` to `datetime.now(UTC)` at the single creation site (line 264) which propagates through `calculateParameterStatistics(analysisDate=analysisDate, ...)` to every ParameterStatistics.analysisDate. Net: same canonical string across all rows in one analysis, identical to the prior datetime-grouping semantics. Live at `src/pi/analysis/engine.py::StatisticsEngine._storeStatistics` (US-203). Reusable for any INSERT-loop that writes a grouping key with per-row-computed timestamps.
- **Column-DEFAULT as implicit writer plumbing — schema change instead of 10 per-site edits**: US-195 needed to tag every INSERT into 5 capture tables (realtime_data / connection_log / statistics / calibration_sessions / profiles) with a new data_source column. The naive approach is to find every INSERT site (10+ writers across data/helpers.py, obd_connection.py, drive/detector.py, shutdown/command_core.py, engine.py, session.py, switcher.py, etc.) and add `data_source='real'` to each. Expensive + fragile — future writers forget, code review misses one, the "default" drifts. Better: push the default DOWN to the schema via `data_source TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT 'real' CHECK (data_source IN (...))`. SQLite's DEFAULT takes over on any INSERT that omits the column; the CHECK rejects wrong values at insert time (cheaper than filtering at read time); the migration helper applies the column via ALTER TABLE ADD COLUMN (SQLite backfills the default into every existing row in place). Now the ONLY writers that need code changes are the non-default ones — replay harness passes 'replay', fixture loader passes 'fixture'. Test fixtures that tag 'fixture' become explicit but the other 10+ live-path writers stay untouched. On the sync path, `getDeltaRows` already does SELECT *, so the column rides through to the server without a serialization edit. The server mirrors the same DEFAULT via SQLAlchemy `server_default=DATA_SOURCE_DEFAULT`. Net: 1 schema change + 1 migration helper + 1 sync-API None-coercion = feature shipped; no per-writer audit. Live at `src/pi/obdii/data_source.py::DATA_SOURCE_COLUMN_DDL` + `src/pi/obdii/database_schema.py` (US-195). Reusable any time a new per-row attribute needs to fan out to many writers.
- **Idempotent ALTER TABLE ADD COLUMN inside initialize() — one code path for fresh + migrated DBs**: US-195 added `data_source` to 5 capture tables. Fresh installs pick it up via the schema DDL's new column. Existing Pi SQLite files (Session 23 has 149 real rows + physics_sim baggage) need the column added in place. The pattern: write a migration helper `ensureDataSourceColumn(conn, tableName)` that checks `PRAGMA table_info(tableName)` for the column, runs `ALTER TABLE ... ADD COLUMN data_source TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT 'real' CHECK (...)` if missing, no-ops if present, no-ops if the table itself doesn't exist yet (first-boot ordering). Call the migration AFTER the schema-creation loop inside `ObdDatabase.initialize()` so the one initialize code path handles both the "fresh DB, schema has the column already" case (helper is a no-op) and the "legacy DB, schema already created before the column existed" case (helper adds it). SQLite applies DEFAULT to every existing row as part of the ADD COLUMN — no backfill UPDATE is needed or scripted. Second call on same DB is a no-op (column present). Tests cover: fresh DB has column (via schema), legacy DB gets column added (via migration), migration is idempotent (running twice produces single column), initialize() upgrades a pre-migration file on disk. Live at `src/pi/obdii/data_source.py::ensureDataSourceColumn` + `src/pi/obdii/database.py::initialize` (US-195). Reusable for any "add column to SQLite table across fleet of existing files" task where Alembic is overkill.
- **Bit-for-bit deterministic SQLite fixtures — VACUUM + sort sqlite_sequence + no wall-clock + closed-form values**: US-191's `seed_pi_fixture.py` proves you can generate a SQLite file whose SHA256 is stable across runs. Four ingredients: (1) every value comes from a pure function of (driveIndex, paramIndex, sampleIndex) — `math.sin(2*pi*sampleIdx/period + 0.37*driveIdx)` beats a seeded Random because you never need to worry about Random's implementation drifting between Python versions. (2) Every timestamp is `_BASE_ISO + timedelta(seconds=offset)` where `_BASE_ISO = "2026-04-19 08:00:00"` is a constant — never `datetime.now()` or anything that reads the wall clock, including DEFAULT CURRENT_TIMESTAMP on `created_at` columns (set explicitly in the INSERT to override). (3) After inserts, `DELETE FROM sqlite_sequence; INSERT ... ORDER BY name` to rewrite the auto-rowid counters in a deterministic physical order (SQLite's planner is free to reorder executemany batches). (4) `conn.execute("VACUUM")` at the end compacts the file — without it, two runs can produce different free-page layouts with the same logical data. Combined, two `buildFixture(same_spec, tmp_path/'X.db')` invocations produce byte-identical output verifiable via `hashlib.sha256(path.read_bytes())`. Live at `scripts/seed_pi_fixture.py::buildFixture` (US-191). Reusable for any "checked-into-git fixture" that must diff cleanly in PR review + be a stable dependency of assertion-count tests.
- **Pi-fixture sync_log seeding: explicit rows per IN_SCOPE_TABLES, not empty-by-default**: `sync_log.getHighWaterMark(...)` returns `(0, None, None, 'pending')` for a missing row, so a fixture with an EMPTY sync_log is functionally equivalent to one with every IN_SCOPE_TABLES entry seeded at `last_synced_id=0`. But for fixture-as-documentation purposes, explicit rows beat implicit defaults — any reader can `sqlite3 fixture.db "SELECT * FROM sync_log ORDER BY table_name"` and see the initial state without having to know the default. Iterate `sync_log.IN_SCOPE_TABLES` (sorted for determinism), INSERT one row per table with `(tableName, 0, None, None, 'pending')`. Tests then assert `{r[0] for r in rows} == sync_log.IN_SCOPE_TABLES` so adding a new in-scope table forces a fixture regeneration + test-update loop. Pattern at `scripts/seed_pi_fixture.py::_primeSyncLog` (US-191). Reusable for any fixture that has a bookkeeping-table whose "default state" is visually ambiguous (empty table vs. primed table both work until you want to see it).
- **Multi-table Pi-shape fixtures must include ALL production tables, not just the ones with data**: SyncClient's `pushDelta(tableName, ...)` runs `SELECT COUNT(*) FROM {tableName} WHERE id > ?` for every table in `sync_log.IN_SCOPE_TABLES`, and sync_now.py's `--dry-run` path iterates the same set. If the fixture only populates realtime_data/connection_log/statistics (what the old server-side `seed_scenarios.py` built), the 5 placeholder tables (`profiles`, `vehicle_info`, `ai_recommendations`, `alert_log`, `calibration_sessions`) don't exist in the fixture and the first SELECT blows up with "no such table". Applying `ALL_SCHEMAS` + `ALL_INDEXES` from `src/pi/obdii/database_schema.py` gets you ALL 11 production tables (incl. the 3 out-of-sync-scope ones: static_data, battery_log, power_log) for free, plus `sync_log.initDb(conn)` adds the bookkeeping table. Empty tables cost ~50 bytes each; the fix is cheap and avoids the "SyncClient choked because the fixture was minimal" trap. Live at `scripts/seed_pi_fixture.py::_createSchema` (US-191). Reusable for any test fixture that's consumed by code which iterates a registry of tables.
- **sh-driver delegation with --keep-service-stopped + triple record_pass/fail for merged step blocks**: when deprecating an old 7-step driver by rewriting steps 1-3 to delegate to a new 8-step driver, the old driver still has a 7-element STEP_RESULTS array for summary output. Three options: (a) collapse to 5 elements + re-number STEP_NAMES — big refactor, risks breaking the summary contract. (b) ignore the gap, print "Step 1-3" as one banner — looks fine in the CLI but the summary array has only 4 records, counting gets weird. (c) emit three `record_pass` (or three `record_fail`, or three `record_skipped`) for the collapsed block so the array stays 7 wide — summary math unchanged, just a visual "inherited from step 1" note for the duplicate entries. Chose (c). Also: the outer driver's `--skip-simulator` semantics carry over — triple `record_skipped` means "all three merged steps were skipped by user request", one `--skip-simulator` skip on a collapsed block would be a confusing single-line "SKIPPED" for a 3-step gap. Applied to `scripts/validate_pi_to_server.sh` (US-191 deprecation). Reusable for any bash driver that's being refactored to delegate steps to a sub-driver while preserving existing summary-array semantics.
- **Bash driver testing via Python subprocess.run + --dry-run flag + _skipWithoutBash**: to test a bash driver in the Python-pytest suite, invoke it via `subprocess.run([shutil.which("bash"), str(driverPath), *args], capture_output=True, text=True, timeout=60)` and drive the behavior branches with `--dry-run` so no SSH/SCP/production actions happen. Bash cold-start is cheap (unlike Windows Store Python's ~30s cold-start), so the 60s timeout covers suite-wide CPU saturation. Use `@pytest.mark.skipif(shutil.which("bash") is None, reason="...")` as a class decorator to cleanly skip the entire test class on any hypothetical bash-less CI runner without erroring collection. Assertion shapes: exit-code tests (`result.returncode == 0/1/2`), stdout-contains tests (help text, dry-run markers), stderr-contains tests for error paths, and a step-ordering test that walks the stdout once with `cursor = stdout.find(nextHeader, cursor)` to catch missing + reordered steps. Live at `tests/scripts/test_replay_pi_fixture_sh.py` (US-191). Reusable for any bash driver that's going to grow new flags or steps over time.
- **ruff treats `.sh` files as Python syntax-errors — don't pass .sh paths**: running `ruff check scripts/foo.sh` surfaces cascading "invalid-syntax" errors because ruff has no content-sniffing and file extensions drive the parser. Passing `scripts/` (the whole dir) is safe — ruff's default include-list excludes .sh. Passing explicit .sh paths breaks the run. Lesson: keep `ruff check` invocations restricted to Python-path patterns (`src/ tests/` or explicit `.py` files). For bash-specific lint, add shellcheck to the pipeline (not yet part of `make lint`). Caught in US-191 when running `ruff check` on the driver + tests in one command.
- **Tri-valued subprocess-shellout signal to distinguish "infra unavailable" from "infra ran, said no"**: US-188's `_readSsidViaIwgetid()` needs to answer THREE distinct things, not two. (a) `iwgetid` binary missing / subprocess timed out / OSError — return `None` — caller maps to UNKNOWN. (b) `iwgetid` ran, non-zero exit (not connected to any WiFi) — return empty string `""` — caller maps to AWAY (deterministic "not home"). (c) `iwgetid` ran, zero exit, stdout has an SSID — return the stripped string. Two-valued helpers that collapse (a) and (b) to a single None-or-missing signal destroy the orchestrator's ability to pick a smart fallback (UNKNOWN "retry later" vs AWAY "definitely not home -> don't try to sync"). Pattern: catch infra errors explicitly (`FileNotFoundError`, `subprocess.TimeoutExpired`, `OSError`) -> None; check `returncode != 0` -> "" (or analogous empty-but-deterministic signal); otherwise return the parsed value. Live at `src/pi/network/home_detector.py::_readSsidViaIwgetid` (US-188). Reusable for any detector that shells out to a Linux tool that might be absent OR might run-and-say-no.
- **Subnet membership with zone-id IPv6 addresses — strip the `%scope` suffix before `ipaddress.ip_address()`**: `hostname -I` on a Linux Pi with multiple interfaces emits IPv4 AND IPv6 addresses, and link-local IPv6 comes back with a zone identifier like `fe80::1%wlan0`. Python's `ipaddress.ip_address('fe80::1%wlan0')` raises `ValueError` because RFC 4007 zone-ids aren't parsed by the stdlib. Pattern: `bare = raw.split('%', 1)[0]` before constructing the address. Quiet no-op on IPv4 (no `%`). Live at `src/pi/network/home_detector.py::_hasIpInHomeSubnet` (US-188). Reusable for any tool that ingests `hostname -I` / `ip -o addr` output.
- **State-transition logging on a bookkeeping object — baseline on first call, compare on every subsequent call**: a detector that polls state and must log transitions (NOT every observation) needs a single `_previousState: HomeNetworkState | None = None` attribute and a `_maybeLogTransition(newState)` method. First call: `if self._previousState is None: self._previousState = newState; return` — no log, just establish baseline. Subsequent calls: `if newState != self._previousState: logger.info("state changed: %s -> %s", self._previousState.value, newState.value); self._previousState = newState`. Same-state polling stays silent. Tests cover all three cases: first-call-silent, change-logs-once, same-state-thrice-silent. Pattern at `src/pi/network/home_detector.py::HomeNetworkDetector._maybeLogTransition` (US-188). Reusable for any polling-based state tracker.
- **Shellout + HTTP injection seams in ONE constructor for a multi-boundary detector**: US-188's `HomeNetworkDetector` needs to mock THREE external boundaries to be Windows-testable — iwgetid (WiFi SSID), hostname -I (local IPs), and urllib.urlopen (server ping). Pattern: constructor takes `ssidReader: Callable[[], str | None] | None = None`, `ipReader: Callable[[], list[str]] | None = None`, `httpOpener: Callable[..., Any] | None = None`, plus `apiKey: str | None = None`. Production defaults: `ssidReader or _readSsidViaIwgetid`, `ipReader or _readLocalIps`, `httpOpener or urllib.request.urlopen`. Tests pass pure-python lambdas/fakes that never shell out and never open sockets. Mirrors US-149's `httpOpener + sleep` pattern but generalizes to N boundaries. Live at `src/pi/network/home_detector.py::HomeNetworkDetector.__init__` (US-188). Reusable for any detector class that needs to aggregate signals from several tool-shellouts + HTTP.
- **CIDR validation in a config validator belongs AT the validator, not at the consumer**: US-188's `pi.homeNetwork.subnet` is free-form config (`"10.27.27.0/24"` default) that the detector passes to `ipaddress.ip_network(...)`. If the CIDR is bogus, that call raises `ValueError`. Options: (a) let the consumer handle it and return False on bad CIDR — detector has to guard every lookup and a misconfigured home subnet silently becomes "never at home". (b) validate at config-load time — `try: ipaddress.ip_network(subnet, strict=False); except ValueError: raise ConfigValidationError(...)` — operator sees the error the moment the config is loaded, not at shutdown time when the orchestrator is trying to decide what to do. Chose (b). Validator still has a defensive-try/except for (a) as a belt-and-braces measure (test covers both), but the primary truth-check is at load. Pattern at `src/common/config/validator.py::_validateHomeNetwork` (US-188). Reusable for any config field that has a syntactic validity check that the consumer would otherwise have to do.
- **Parameter-name decoder registry with separate obd-command binding — map user-facing names to (underlying command, PID, decoder) and branch at the query seam**: US-199 needed 6 new Mode 01 PIDs + 1 adapter command to enter the Pi poll set under Spool-facing parameter_names (FUEL_SYSTEM_STATUS, MIL_ON, DTC_COUNT, RUNTIME_SEC, BAROMETRIC_KPA, BATTERY_V, O2_BANK1_SENSOR2_V) that don't map 1:1 to python-obd's command names (FUEL_STATUS, STATUS, RUN_TIME, BAROMETRIC_PRESSURE, ELM_VOLTAGE, O2_B1S2). Two naive options: (a) fork `obd_parameters.py` and add aliases — forces every downstream consumer (display, alerts, analysis) to learn the alias table. (b) rename python-obd commands at import time — monkey-patches a third-party library. Both fight the architecture. Better: a module-level dict `PARAMETER_DECODERS: dict[str, ParameterDecoderEntry]` where each entry carries `(parameterName, obdCommand, pidCode, decoder, description)`. The query path in `ObdDataLogger.queryParameter` checks the registry FIRST — if the parameterName is registered, use entry.obdCommand for the python-obd lookup and entry.decoder for the response-to-LoggedReading transform; otherwise fall through to the legacy getattr(obdlib.commands, parameterName) path. Two big wins: (1) new PIDs never require touching downstream consumers — they just ask for the Spool-facing name and get a LoggedReading. (2) enum-shaped and multi-field PIDs (STATUS → MIL+DTC, FUEL_STATUS → tuple, O2_B1S2 → (voltage, STFT) tuple) get per-entry decoder callbacks that normalize to (valueNumeric, unit, optional textLabel) without the generic `_extractValue` ever seeing the raw shape. For the enum case (FUEL_SYSTEM_STATUS with REAL-only schema) the textLabel lands in `reading.unit` (TEXT column) — analysts read "CL" directly while value keeps the numeric grouping key. Live at `src/pi/obdii/decoders.py::PARAMETER_DECODERS` + `src/pi/obdii/data/logger.py::queryParameter` (US-199). Reusable for any situation where domain vocabulary (what the user / analyst names things) needs to decouple from the underlying protocol vocabulary (what the wire-level library calls things).
- **Support-probe cache as a precondition gate — probe once, check many, fall back to permissive**: US-199's acceptance demanded silent-skip of unsupported PIDs WITHOUT dispatching an OBD query that would just return null (K-line round trip = 150-200ms wasted per unsupported PID per poll cycle). Pattern: a standalone `pid_probe.py` module exposes `SupportedPidSet` (dataclass wrapping `set[str]` of lowercase two-hex-char codes + `fallbackAllowAll: bool` + `alwaysSupported()` factory) and `probeSupportedPids(obdConnection) -> SupportedPidSet` that reads python-obd's auto-probed `supported_commands` at connection-open time. The probe normalizes PIDs lazily via `__post_init__` so direct constructor calls (`SupportedPidSet({'0x0C'})`) and probe-derived sets both work. `ObdConnection.connect()` calls `_runSupportedPidProbe()` post-success inside a best-effort try/except (probe failure NEVER fails the connection — falls back to alwaysSupported). The data logger's `queryParameter` consults `self.connection.supportedPids` via `_assertPidSupported(entry)`: Mode 01 entries raise `ParameterNotSupportedError` if their pidCode isn't in the set; adapter entries (pidCode=None) always bypass the gate; a missing cache (legacy ObdConnection instances, tests that inject a FakeConnection without setting supportedPids) treats as "always supported" for BC. Net: three-state gate — explicit-supported proceeds, explicit-unsupported raises pre-dispatch, no-cache-or-probe-failed falls through to null-response silent-skip downstream. Live at `src/pi/obdii/pid_probe.py::probeSupportedPids` + `src/pi/obdii/obd_connection.py::_runSupportedPidProbe` + `src/pi/obdii/data/logger.py::_assertPidSupported` (US-199). Reusable any time a protocol's pre-negotiated capability set should gate runtime dispatch (e.g., HTTP feature headers, gRPC reflection-advertised methods, database server version feature flags).
- **Encode enum as (value=float_code + unit=text_label) when schema forces REAL NOT NULL**: Spool wanted `realtime_data.parameter_name='FUEL_SYSTEM_STATUS'` to carry OL/CL/OL-drive/OL-fault/CL-fault. The schema has `value REAL NOT NULL` (enforced by B-037 onward; migrating to TEXT would break 149 real rows + all downstream analytics queries that do AVG/MAX/MIN on value). Easy-but-wrong solutions: (a) store code only ('2.0') — analysts lose human-readability, every query needs a JOIN to an enum table the codebase doesn't have. (b) migrate value to TEXT — cascading break across analytics layer. (c) split into two parameter_name rows ('FUEL_SYSTEM_STATUS_CODE' + 'FUEL_SYSTEM_STATUS_TEXT') — doubles row count + joins complexity. Right answer: use the existing `unit` TEXT column (normally "rpm", "°C", "kPa") as a dual-purpose slot for enum parameters. Decoder returns `DecodedReading(valueNumeric=2.0, unit='fuel_status', textLabel='CL')`; the LoggedReading wrapper writes `reading.unit = decoded.textLabel if decoded.textLabel else decoded.unit`. Net: `SELECT value, unit FROM realtime_data WHERE parameter_name='FUEL_SYSTEM_STATUS'` returns `(2.0, 'CL')` — both machine-groupable (MAX grouping on numeric code is trivial) AND human-readable without a lookup table. Downside: "unit" semantics drift from the literal "unit of measurement" intent for enum rows, but this is cheap to document in grounded-knowledge.md. Live at `src/pi/obdii/decoders.py::decodeFuelSystemStatus` + `src/pi/obdii/data/logger.py::_queryViaDecoder` (US-199). Reusable for any schema-frozen value column that needs to carry occasional categorical state.
- **SDL_VIDEODRIVER=dummy at module import-time vs pi_only fixture monkeypatch.delenv for real-framebuffer tests**: when a test file mixes off-Pi smoke tests (that MUST use the SDL dummy driver so CI doesn't try to open a window) with `pi_only` tests (that MUST use the real framebuffer to prove the Pi's HDMI actually works), put `os.environ.setdefault("SDL_VIDEODRIVER", "dummy")` at the TOP of the module (before `import pygame`) AND add a `@pytest.fixture(autouse=True)` on the pi_only class that calls `monkeypatch.delenv("SDL_VIDEODRIVER", raising=False)`. Without the delenv, pi_only tests also resolve to the dummy driver and silently "pass" without ever touching the real display — looks like a pass, actually tests nothing. Live at `tests/pi/display/test_hdmi_render.py::TestLiveHdmiDisplay._enableRealFramebuffer` (US-183). Reusable for any pygame/SDL mixed-environment test module.
- **Dict-based exit flag for signal handlers in script-scope render loops**: a bare `nonlocal exitRequested` inside a SIGTERM/SIGINT handler requires plumbing from the handler back up to the render loop's scope, which is ugly when the handler is registered from a helper function. Clean pattern: `_installSignalHandlers()` returns a dict (`{"exitRequested": False}`), handlers mutate `state["exitRequested"] = True`, the render loop polls `if exitFlag["exitRequested"]: break`. No `nonlocal`, no module globals, the handler state is a plain object the caller owns. Live at `scripts/render_primary_screen_live.py::_installSignalHandlers` (US-183). Reusable for any signal-driven exit path in a Python CLI.
- **Triangle-wave parameter sweep as a visible render-loop heartbeat**: when a CIO needs to confirm visually that a render loop is not stalled, a linear triangle sweep of one gauge (e.g. RPM 800->6500->800 over 4s) is much more legible than a sine wave, a random walk, or a scripted scenario — the gauge needle moves in straight lines with obvious reversals at the endpoints. Implementation: `position = cycle * 2 if cycle < 0.5 else (1 - cycle) * 2` where `cycle = (elapsed % period) / period`. O(1), no state, deterministic. Keep other gauges static so the sweep is the one unambiguous animation. Live at `scripts/render_primary_screen_live.py::_currentRpm` (US-183). Reusable for any "prove the loop is alive" validation harness.
- **Per-tier display color palette via a dedicated `theme.py`, not a mutation of the existing severity→color mapping**: US-165 needed blue/white/orange/red (spec 2.4) while US-164 basic tier uses white/yellow/red. Tempting shortcut: change `primary_screen._severityToColor` to orange for CAUTION and add a blue branch. That would silently regress every US-164 test that passed with yellow. Better: introduce `src/pi/display/theme.py` with `advancedTierSeverityToColor(severity) -> str` + an `ADVANCED_TIER_COLORS: dict[AlertSeverity, str]` constant, callers pick the right mapper per tier. Basic-tier file stays byte-compatible with Sprint 10; advanced-tier file imports theme and applies it. Pattern applies any time a new UI surface wants a different look over the same underlying severity/state enum. Live at `src/pi/display/theme.py::advancedTierSeverityToColor` + `src/pi/display/screens/primary_screen_advanced.py::_valueColor` (US-165).
- **Pure-data `LayoutElement` pipeline scales cleanly to new tiers**: US-164 established `buildXScreenState -> computeXLayout -> list[LayoutElement]` where LayoutElement is a kind+region+geometry dataclass and the pygame renderer walks the list. US-165 reused this verbatim — new dataclasses (`AdvancedTierHeader` with `ConnectivityIndicators`, `GaugeHistory`, `AdvancedTierFooter`), new layout function, SAME `LayoutElement` type, SAME `primary_renderer._drawElement` dispatcher. Zero new primitive types needed. For any future tier (touch overlay, detail screens) the pattern is: new dataclass → new layout composer → append to list[LayoutElement]. The renderer is a union of primitives; tiers are orthogonal. Live at `src/pi/display/screens/primary_screen_advanced.py::computeAdvancedTierLayout` (US-165).
- **Inject `nowSeconds` into relative-time formatters for deterministic tests**: `formatLastSyncAgo(lastSyncSeconds, nowSeconds)` takes both timestamps as arguments rather than calling `time.time()` internally. Tests pass a fixed `nowSeconds=1_700_000_000.0` and vary `lastSyncSeconds` to cover never/just-now/Nm/Nh/Nd/future cases without mocking. The outer renderer (`_appendFooter`) applies the `time.time()` default via `footer.nowSeconds if footer.nowSeconds is not None else time.time()` — the helper stays pure. Reusable for any "N ago" / "in N" formatter. Live at `src/pi/display/screens/primary_screen_advanced.py::formatLastSyncAgo` (US-165).
- **Offscreen pygame via `SDL_VIDEODRIVER=dummy` for CI/screenshot generation**: spoofing the SDL video driver with `os.environ.setdefault('SDL_VIDEODRIVER', 'dummy')` before importing pygame lets `pygame.Surface((W, H))` + `pygame.image.save(surface, path)` produce a PNG without any display server — works on CI, SSH sessions, and GUI-less Windows test runners. `pygame.font.init()` still works under the dummy driver. Contrast with `pygame.display.set_mode()` which requires a real framebuffer. The screenshot-generation script can live in `scripts/` next to other CLI drivers and be run from anywhere. Live at `scripts/render_advanced_tier_sample.py` (US-165). Reusable for any pygame-rendered fixture or regression screenshot.
- **Statistics-table reduction for "last N drives min/max"**: each completed drive writes one row per parameter to the `statistics` table with `min_value`, `max_value`, `analysis_date`. To aggregate "min/max across the last N drives", the query is PER-PARAMETER `SELECT min_value, max_value FROM statistics WHERE parameter_name = ? ORDER BY analysis_date DESC LIMIT N` followed by an in-Python reduction (`min(per-row mins), max(per-row maxes)`) — NOT a single global `LIMIT N` over all params, because different drives observe different parameter sets and a global limit gives asymmetric coverage. NULL-row tolerant (legacy rows with NULL min/max get skipped rather than poisoning the reduction). Live at `src/pi/data/recent_stats.py::queryRecentMinMax` (US-165). Reusable for any "last-N bucketed aggregation by time" query over a pre-computed stats table.
- **Post-directory-rename, sweep BOTH dotted-import and pathlib-slash forms — `\bpi\.obd\b` sed regex does NOT match `/ "pi" / "obd" /`**: US-187 renamed `src/pi/obd/` -> `src/pi/obdii/` and did a bulk `\bpi\.obd\b -> pi.obdii` sed across ~90 *.py files. First full-suite run was 2063 passed + 5 failed — all 5 failures in tests/pi/simulator/test_scenario_arm.py:77 where the test file builds a path as `Path(__file__).resolve().parents[3] / "src" / "pi" / "obd" / "simulator" / "scenarios"`. The dotted-import regex missed it because the string "obd" there is a standalone quoted path segment, not part of a `pi.obd` token. Moral: after any directory rename, run TWO sweeps — `grep -rn '\bpi\.obd\b' --include="*.py"` (catches dotted imports + `logging.getLogger("pi.obd.orchestrator")` + `'pi.obd.X'` string literals) AND `grep -rn '"obd"\|/ *"obd"' --include="*.py"` (catches pathlib-style `/ "obd" /` segments anywhere the test or script builds a package path explicitly). Also grep for `pi/obd/` as a bare path substring in case forward-slash string paths exist. The pathlib form is the sneaky one — it compiles fine (pathlib doesn't validate the directory exists at import time), only fails at test-time when `open()` resolves to the now-deleted path. Live example + fix at `tests/pi/simulator/test_scenario_arm.py:77` (US-187). Reusable for any future `src/pi/X -> src/pi/Y` rename or similar directory move.
- **Stdlib ThreadingHTTPServer as a mocked-server fixture for Pi↔server HTTP integration tests**: US-166's e2e pipeline test needs a server that accepts POST /api/v1/sync and asserts on received payloads, WITHOUT pulling in httpx_mock, respx, pytest-httpserver, or starting a real FastAPI app (which would drag sqlalchemy + all server deps onto the Pi's test dependency graph). Pattern: a `BaseHTTPRequestHandler` subclass with a `do_POST` method that reads the body, validates X-API-Key, and records the JSON payload into a thread-safe `_MockStore`. Bind via `ThreadingHTTPServer(('127.0.0.1', _findFreePort()), _Handler)` + `threading.Thread(target=server.serve_forever, daemon=True)`. Attach the store to `server.mockStore` as a class-level monkey-patch so the handler can read it via `self.server.mockStore`. Clean shutdown: `server.shutdown(); server.server_close(); thread.join(timeout=2)`. Ephemeral port (`socket.bind(('127.0.0.1', 0))` + `getsockname()[1]`) means tests run in parallel without port collisions. This exercises the exact same `urllib.request.urlopen` path SyncClient uses in production — more realistic than injecting an httpOpener mock. Live at `tests/integration/test_pi_to_server_e2e.py::_MockSyncHandler` + `_MockStore` + `_startMockServer` (US-166). Reusable for any Pi-tier client that POSTs JSON and needs an end-to-end assertion without external deps.
- **7-step live-validation bash driver with PASS/FAIL-per-step + broken-layer identification**: US-166's `scripts/validate_pi_to_server.sh` is the CIO-facing live counterpart to the CI test. Pattern: declare parallel arrays `STEP_NAMES` and `STEP_RESULTS`, call `record_pass` / `record_fail "reason"` / `record_skipped "reason"` after each step, emit a structured summary at the end. For a sprint-exit driver where the CIO needs to identify which layer is broken, the step numbers become the diagnostic: document "step 3 FAIL = SyncClient/config/auth; step 4 FAIL = server /api/v1/sync or MariaDB upsert; step 5-6 FAIL = scripts/report.py; step 7 FAIL = display". Three flags cover the needed shapes: `--duration N` (tunable simulator run), `--skip-simulator` (validate existing DB state), `--dry-run` (print plan without touching anything). Credentials harvested via a tiny `loadEnvFile('.env')` snippet inside `$SERVER_VENV/bin/python -c ...` over ssh rather than keying into the driver. Exit codes: 0=all PASS, 1=any FAIL, 2=SSH gate or misuse. Pattern at `scripts/validate_pi_to_server.sh` (US-166). Reusable for any cross-machine validation driver where a human operator needs to pinpoint which tier broke.
- **`syncClientFactory(config) -> SyncClient` injection seam for CLIs that wrap a fat service class**: US-154's scripts/sync_now.py needs to exercise 4 PushStatus × 3 exit-code paths × banner/totals formatting — doing that against a real SyncClient would require a full Pi SQLite + mocked HTTP on every test. Cleaner pattern: give main(argv, *, syncClientFactory=None) an optional factory hook; production defaults to `_defaultSyncClientFactory(config) -> SyncClient(config)`, tests pass `_factoryReturning(_FakeSyncClient(scripted_results))`. The fake exposes the minimum duck-typed surface the CLI reads: `.baseUrl`, `.batchSize`, `.dbPath`, `.pushAllDeltas() -> list[PushResult]`, plus a `pushAllDeltasCalls` counter so --dry-run can be proven to not push. 14 tests all run in 14s without a single socket or sqlite connection. Reusable for any script that's an argparse wrapper around a service-layer class. Live at `scripts/sync_now.py::main` + `_defaultSyncClientFactory` + `tests/scripts/test_sync_now.py::_FakeSyncClient` (US-154).
- **CLI exit-code logic via a tri-valued `_overallStatus(results)` helper, separate from per-row formatting**: when a CLI fans out N independent operations and needs a single exit code + summary word, split the decision into a pure function that takes `list[PushResult]` and returns one of OK/FAILED/DISABLED. Rule: FAILED if any result failed (exit 1); DISABLED if every result is DISABLED (exit 0, distinct from OK because the operator may have turned off sync intentionally); OK otherwise (mixed OK+EMPTY + all-EMPTY both count as OK, because "nothing to sync" is a successful run). Keep the helper out of main() so tests can cover the 3-way decision without launching the whole CLI; keep per-row formatting in a second helper so the summary word can change independent of row format. Pattern at `scripts/sync_now.py::_overallStatus` (US-154).
- **"Preserve-HWM on failure" idiom — re-write the mark with its current value + status='failed' + batchId so the row updates without advancing**: US-149's data-integrity invariant says `sync_log.last_synced_id` must NOT move on a failed push, but we DO want the diagnostic trail (which batch attempted it, when, status=failed) visible in the sync_log for operator debugging. The `updateHighWaterMark(conn, tableName, lastId, batchId, status='failed')` call uses the CURRENT `lastId` (read moments earlier) as the new value — SQLite's UPSERT rewrites all four columns, but since `last_synced_id` is set to the same value it already held, it's observationally unchanged. Next push re-reads the same lastId and re-sends the same rows. Pattern applicable any time a client needs to persist "attempted + failed" telemetry without advancing a protected cursor. Live in `src/pi/sync/client.py::SyncClient.pushDelta` (US-149).
- **HTTP retry classifier: 4xx (except 429) must fail-IMMEDIATELY with zero retries, retrying is actively harmful**: a persistent 401/403 means the API key is wrong; a persistent 422 means the payload is malformed. Retrying either just hammers the server with the same broken request and delays failure by `sum(backoffDelays)` seconds. Correct classifier: `HTTPError code >= 500 -> retry; code == 429 -> retry; 400 <= code < 500 (not 429) -> raise _PushFailure immediately without entering the retry loop`. The 429 exception to the 4xx rule is because rate limits ARE transient — backoff gives the bucket time to refill. Pattern codified in `src/pi/sync/client.py::_isRetryableHttpStatus` + `_postBatchWithRetry` (US-149). Tests explicitly verify `len(opener.calls) == 1` for 401/403 — any retry on those is a bug.
- **Injection seams for retry-with-backoff code: httpOpener + sleep both get knobs, tests finish in ms**: US-149's SyncClient retries up to 4 times with real wall-clock sleeps of 1s/2s/4s by default — 7s per failure test if left alone. Every failure-path test would add ~7 seconds to the fast suite, and the test count balloons fast (5 failure tests = 35s). Fix: constructor takes optional `httpOpener=None` (defaults to `urllib.request.urlopen`) AND `sleep=None` (defaults to `time.sleep`). Tests inject a `noSleep` stub that records the delay values without actually sleeping; separate assertions prove the backoff schedule was [1.0, 2.0, 4.0] without waiting for it. Fan-out: the same dual-injection pattern is reusable for any future "retry with backoff" client. Bonus: the noSleep fixture doubles as a regression check — if the backoff schedule drifts (say someone adds a jitter multiplier without bumping the test expectation), `assert noSleep.calls == [1.0, 2.0, 4.0]` catches it. Pattern at `tests/pi/sync/test_sync_client.py::noSleep` + `_successOpener`/`_httpErrorOpener`/`_timeoutOpener`/`_urlErrorOpener` (US-149).
- **urllib.request.Request.header_items() returns capitalized keys — test header assertions must match**: urllib normalizes HTTP header names to capitalized form (first letter uppercase, rest lowercase) when you read them back via `req.header_items()`. A `Request(headers={'X-API-Key': 'value'})` round-trips as `{'X-api-key': 'value'}` — the 'API' part goes lowercase except for the first 'A'. Likewise `Content-Type` -> `Content-type`. This is urllib-specific and tripped the payload-shape test. Pattern: either compare with `.casefold()` or hard-code the urllib-normalized form in test assertions. Affects any test that builds a Request, then reads headers back off it. Live at `tests/pi/sync/test_sync_client.py::test_requestPayload_hasExpectedShape`.
- **urllib.request is good enough for Pi outbound HTTP — no new dep required**: US-149 was ACd to `add requests or httpx if not already present`. Neither is present in requirements-pi.txt. The stdlib `urllib.request` gives: `urlopen(Request(url, data=body, headers={...}, method='POST'), timeout=seconds)` + `urllib.error.HTTPError` (has `.code` / `.reason`) + `urllib.error.URLError`. That covers every network-level thing this client needs: 2xx status = success via context manager; 4xx/5xx = HTTPError; DNS/connect fail = URLError; deadline = TimeoutError. No extra wheel to vendor onto the Pi, no new supply-chain surface. Matches the VIN decoder precedent in agent.md. Pattern choice lives at `src/pi/sync/client.py` module-level imports + `_postBatchWithRetry` loop (US-149).
- **Sprint-flagged data-integrity tests belong at the top of the test file, organized in one class named after the invariant**: US-149 sprint notes explicitly said "Write the failure-path test FIRST." That's usually read as "write the first test first" but the real value is test-file organization: when a future reader opens `test_sync_client.py` 6 months from now and something regresses, the FIRST test failure they see should be the HWM-not-advanced assertion — not a stylistic edge case about header-capitalization. So cluster the critical invariant tests in one class (`TestCriticalInvariantFailedPushDoesNotAdvanceHighWaterMark`) at the top of the file, named loudly enough that pytest's output reads the name in every run. Reusable wherever a sprint spec calls out a "CRITICAL" invariant. Live at `tests/pi/sync/test_sync_client.py`.
- **Post-default semantic validation pass for range/shape constraints on nested config sections**: the existing `DEFAULTS` / `_applyDefaults()` machinery in `ConfigValidator` handles "is the key present"; it does NOT validate numeric ranges or structural shape. For sections with real invariants (`syncTimeoutSeconds > 0`, `batchSize >= 1`, `retryBackoffSeconds` is a list, `retryMaxAttempts >= 0`), add a dedicated `_validateXxx(config)` method invoked from `validate()` AFTER `_applyDefaults()`. Two benefits: (a) defaults are guaranteed populated when your validator runs, so no None-handling at every step; (b) callers get `ConfigValidationError` at load time with the offending dot-path in `missingFields` — rather than a cryptic TypeError three layers deep inside an HTTP client. Pattern established in `src/common/config/validator.py::_validateCompanionService` (US-151).
- **bool-vs-int guard for numeric config fields — `isinstance(True, int)` is True in Python**: a stray JSON `true`/`false` in a numeric field will pass a naive `isinstance(x, (int, float))` check and silently become `1` / `0`. For `syncTimeoutSeconds=true` that means "1-second timeout"; for `batchSize=false` that means "0 rows per request" (likely infinite retries on empty payload). Explicit guard: `if isinstance(v, bool) or not isinstance(v, (int, float)) or v <= 0`. The bool check MUST come first — otherwise the second clause accepts it. Applied in `_validateCompanionService` (US-151). Pattern reusable for any config validator that mixes numeric and boolean fields.
- **SQLite UPSERT via ON CONFLICT DO UPDATE SET ... FROM excluded**: when a table has a PRIMARY KEY and you want an insert-or-update-with-atomic-multi-field-advance, the idiom is `INSERT INTO t (cols) VALUES (...) ON CONFLICT(pk_col) DO UPDATE SET c1=excluded.c1, c2=excluded.c2, ...`. The `excluded` pseudo-table is SQLite's handle for the proposed row. One statement, one transaction, no read-then-write race. Used in `src/pi/data/sync_log.py::updateHighWaterMark` (US-148) to advance last_synced_id + last_synced_at + last_batch_id + status together — any failure rolls all four back, no partial state.
- **Table-name whitelist IS the SQL-injection guard when the table is a SQL identifier**: `?`-parameter binding works for values but NOT for identifiers. A function that takes `tableName: str` and interpolates it into SQL (`f"SELECT * FROM {tableName}"`) is intrinsically unsafe unless the caller is trusted OR the name is validated against a closed whitelist. Pattern: `_validateTable(tableName)` against a `frozenset` of known-safe names, raise ValueError otherwise. Doubled as a scope-check in US-148 (rejects battery_log/power_log even though those tables exist on the Pi — just not in sync scope). Test literally uses the injection string `'malicious; DROP TABLE realtime_data;--'` and asserts (a) ValueError is raised AND (b) the target table is still intact afterward.
- **`src/pi/data/` is the Pi-tier data-layer package, separate from `src/pi/obd/`**: sync bookkeeping (sync_log) and future cache layers live here, not inside the OBD DB module. The two packages both own SQLite state but evolve independently — OBD schema changes don't drag the sync contract through the same module, and vice versa. The PM scope on US-148 made this explicit by listing `src/pi/obd/` in doNotTouch. Callers of `src.pi.data.sync_log` pass in an open `sqlite3.Connection`; the module never manages connection lifetime.
- **CAVEAT on EXT5V as the AC-vs-battery signal**: the prior US-180 pattern ("EXT5V via vcgencmd threshold at 4.5V") assumed the HAT does NOT regulate the Pi-side 5V rail under UPS-boost. The Geekworm X1209 specifically VIOLATES that assumption — it regulates the rail to ~5V in both wall-power and UPS-boost modes so EXT5V reads identical in both cases (I-015, Session 21 CIO unplug drill, US-184 resolution). EXT5V is still useful as a "is the HAT delivering power?" diagnostic, but not as a source-detection signal on regulated HATs. For AC-vs-battery on such HATs, see the "VCELL-trend + CRATE-polarity" pattern below. The old Pi 5 PMIC EXT5V pattern remains valid ONLY on HATs that don't regulate (unregulated passthrough) — verify with a physical unplug drill before relying on it.
- **VCELL-trend + CRATE-polarity heuristic for AC-vs-battery on regulated-output UPS HATs** (US-184): when a HAT regulates the Pi-side rail (so EXT5V is invariant), derive source from the LiPo's own discharge signal. Two inputs:
  (1) CRATE polarity — MAX17048 register 0x16, signed 16-bit big-endian, 0.208 %/hr/LSB. If readable AND < threshold (e.g. < -0.05 %/hr), cell is discharging -> BATTERY. Not all chip variants populate CRATE (some return 0xFFFF); treat as unavailable then.
  (2) VCELL slope over a rolling window — keep a time-pruned buffer of (t_monotonic, vcell_volts, soc) samples populated by the polling loop. Compute first-vs-last slope in V/min (O(1), noise-tolerant enough for a 60s window); < threshold (e.g. < -0.02 V/min) -> BATTERY. Linear regression is overkill; the discharge step-change is dominant.
  Decision tree: CRATE < threshold -> BATTERY. Else slope < threshold -> BATTERY. Else EXTERNAL. If neither signal available (no CRATE, <2 history samples) -> fall through to the last cached source, initially EXTERNAL. The cached source prevents false-positive flips during the first few polling ticks and during temporary "no evidence" windows.
  Implementation notes: inject `monotonicClock=Callable` for deterministic tests. Prune buffer by wall-time comparison (not maxlen) so the buffer is decoupled from pollInterval. Acquire a lock around buffer mutations — `getPowerSource()` is called from both the polling thread and main-thread telemetry calls. Guard CRATE reads through a `_safeReadCrate()` wrapper that converts UpsMonitorError/UpsNotAvailableError to None so a transient I2C hiccup on register 0x16 doesn't mask a valid VCELL-slope decision. Pattern at `src/pi/hardware/ups_monitor.py::{getPowerSource, recordHistorySample, _computeVcellSlopeVoltsPerMinute}` (US-184).
- **Pi 5 PMIC EXT5V_V via vcgencmd is the external-power signal when the HAT has no AC/battery sense pin AND does NOT regulate the Pi-side rail**: the MAX17048 fuel gauge on the Geekworm X1209 tracks the LiPo cell only — it has no AC-vs-battery pin and no power-source register. The Pi 5 PMIC exposes the USB-C EXT5V rail's voltage via `vcgencmd pmic_read_adc EXT5V_V`, which prints a line like `EXT5V_V volt(24)=5.27558000V`. Extract the voltage with `re.search(r'=\s*([\d.]+)\s*V', stdout)`. Graceful degradation: treat FileNotFoundError (no vcgencmd), TimeoutExpired, and unparseable output as None rather than exceptions. This pattern STILL applies as a diagnostic on regulated HATs (US-184 retains it as `getDiagnosticExt5vVoltage()`), but is NOT the source-detection signal on the X1209 — see the VCELL-trend + CRATE pattern above.
- **Directory-level pytest skip via `collect_ignore_glob` + `importlib.util.find_spec`**:
  when a whole subtree of tests requires an optional dep (e.g. all of
  `tests/server/` needs `sqlalchemy`, which is intentionally absent from
  `requirements-pi.txt`), drop a `conftest.py` in that subdir with:
  ```python
  import importlib.util
  collect_ignore_glob: list[str] = []
  if importlib.util.find_spec('sqlalchemy') is None:
      collect_ignore_glob = ['test_*.py']
  ```
  Pytest silently excludes the whole directory from collection — no
  ``ModuleNotFoundError`` collection errors, no per-file `importorskip`
  boilerplate. Platforms with the dep see zero behavior change. Pattern
  established in `tests/server/conftest.py` (US-182). Way cleaner than
  per-file `pytest.importorskip` at top-of-file — those still trigger the
  underlying `from sqlalchemy import …` line that fails before the skip.
- **Platform-gated pytest marker — `pi_only` pattern**:
  register the marker in `pyproject.toml` + `pytest_configure`, then add a
  `pytest_collection_modifyitems` hook that auto-skips on off-platform:
  ```python
  def _isRunningOnPi() -> bool:
      if os.environ.get('ECLIPSE_PI_HOST') == '1':
          return True
      return sys.platform == 'linux' and platform.machine() == 'aarch64'

  def pytest_collection_modifyitems(config, items):
      if _isRunningOnPi():
          return
      skip = pytest.mark.skip(reason='pi_only: requires Pi hardware; '
                              'set ECLIPSE_PI_HOST=1 to run')
      for item in items:
          if 'pi_only' in item.keywords:
              item.add_marker(skip)
  ```
  Reusable for any platform-specific marker (server_only, wifi_only, etc.).
  Auto-detect + env-var opt-in covers both "runs for free on the target
  host" and "let me force-run anywhere for debugging". Validated three ways
  in US-182: on Pi auto-detect (runs), on Windows default (skips), on
  Windows with ECLIPSE_PI_HOST=1 (runs + fails loudly because not a Pi —
  correct semantics).
- **adafruit_rgb_display 3.11.x breaks on Python 3.13 at import time**:
  the wheel has `def image_to_data(image: Image) -> Any:` at module scope
  but never imports `PIL.Image`. On Python < 3.12, annotations are lazy
  strings and the missing name is never resolved; on Python 3.13, the
  annotation is eagerly evaluated at `def` time and raises `NameError:
  name 'Image' is not defined` — from inside the library itself, before
  the importing code can react. Any `try/except ImportError` around the
  import lets this slip through. Fix: broaden the catch to
  `(ImportError, NameError, AttributeError, NotImplementedError,
  RuntimeError)` so a broken library is treated as "driver not available"
  rather than crashing the hardware-verification script. Applied to
  `scripts/verify_hardware.py` (US-182).
- **Windows Store Python subprocess cold-start > 30s under load**: the
  `python.exe` in the Windows Store is a thin launcher that pages in the
  real interpreter from `%LOCALAPPDATA%\Microsoft\WindowsApps\…` on first
  spawn. Under full-suite CPU load this routinely takes 30-50s just to
  reach `main()`. Tests that `subprocess.run(…, timeout=30)` a Python CLI
  script will fail intermittently on the same test file that passes
  standalone. The root fix is a `timeout` headroom (120s for real CLIs;
  60s only if you're certain the suite won't saturate CPU). Don't chase
  the flake — Sessions 26/27/28 hit this three times before it was
  tracked in US-182's AC #9. Applied to `tests/test_verify_database.py`.
- **MAX17048 word reads need big-endian byte-swap over SMBus**: smbus2
  `read_word_data()` returns little-endian, MAX17048 stores each 16-bit
  register big-endian. For VCELL/SOC/CRATE: read the raw word, then
  `((w & 0xFF) << 8) | ((w >> 8) & 0xFF)` before applying scale factors.
  Without the swap, a full-charge LiPo (~4.2V) reads as ~20V garbage
  (what Rex saw Session 41). If any future code reads a big-endian-only
  I2C chip (MAX17048, many MAX-prefix fuel gauges, some INA2xx variants),
  add the swap at the helper layer — don't duplicate it at every call.
- **Fingerprint an I2C chip by reading VERSION + CONFIG defaults**:
  fastest way to confirm "is this really a MAX17048?" is to read the
  VERSION register (0x08), byte-swap, and compare to the datasheet value.
  Next read CONFIG (0x0C) — MAX17048 boots to 0x971C family. If both
  line up, the chip is confirmed without wiring a logic analyzer. Took
  <60s of SMBus probing Session 41 to identify a chip that had been
  "MAX17048-family (unverified)" in the codebase for three months.
- **A chip's missing register is a spec↔hardware-architecture problem,
  not a code bug**: MAX17048 has no current register and no power-source
  register. US-180's AC #3 (current) and AC #5 (AC-vs-battery) are
  infeasible against this chip — they need either an external sense
  line or a PMIC-based detection (vcgencmd pmic_read_adc EXT5V_V works
  on Pi 5 and doesn't need HAT cooperation). When an AC asks for a
  reading the chip physically can't provide, file a blocker — don't
  fabricate a heuristic to make the test pass.
- **stopCondition is a contract, not a suggestion**: US-180 stopCondition
  #2 said "STOP if UPS reports nonsense — likely driver/calibration
  issue, do not proceed to US-181." The instinct Session 41 was to fix
  the register map in-place because scope said "src/pi/hardware/ (narrow
  — only if bugs surface)." But a register-map rewrite for a different
  chip (4 methods + byte-order + scale factors + tests + spec update)
  is not narrow — it's a chip-semantics rework. Respect both the scope
  and the stopCondition: file the blocker, let PM decide.

- **Mock only the hardware boundary, drive the real code under test**: the
  old tests/test_ups_monitor.py + test_gpio_button.py + test_telemetry_logger.py
  were deleted Feb 2026 (commit de0c34b) as 'mock theatre'. US-180's replacements
  mock ONLY the I2cClient (the real hardware boundary) or inject state directly
  (button._isAvailable = False). The actual UpsMonitor._pollingLoop,
  RotatingFileHandler rotation, gpiozero handlers, sign-extension math, and
  callback wiring are exercised for real. Result: 32 tests that each prove
  observable behavior (exception type, counter state, backup files appear,
  callback called with specific args), not 'mock.method was called'.
- **isAvailable-is-bool is more portable than isAvailable-is-False**: the
  first iteration of the GPIO button tests asserted `isAvailable is False`
  with "onNonPi" in the name. That passed on Windows and failed on the real
  Pi (gpiozero IS available there). Testing `isinstance(button.isAvailable,
  bool)` + forcing `_isAvailable = False` to exercise the unavailable branch
  makes the same test pass on both platforms. Pattern for any test that
  needs to hit a "graceful degradation" path without caring where it runs:
  inject the state flag, don't assume the platform.
- **Pi 5 has phantom I2C buses 13 and 14**: Pi 5's RP1 chip exposes
  /dev/i2c-13 and /dev/i2c-14 in addition to /dev/i2c-1. i2cdetect on 13
  or 14 shows 'ghost' reads at every address (every cell populated) — NOT
  because devices are there, but because those buses have no pull-ups and
  the BCM driver returns success on every address. If a validation ever
  finds a device on bus 13 or 14, verify the same device is actually
  selectable (read a register, check the value) before trusting it.
- **HAT EEPROM is the truth-source for HAT identification**: to tell if a
  GPIO-header board is a HAT-compliant device (with I2C identification)
  vs. a dumb pass-through power board, check `/proc/device-tree/hat/`. If
  the directory doesn't exist, no HAT EEPROM is present, which means the
  board is either unplugged, not a HAT, or defective. Combined with
  i2cdetect -y 1 being empty, that's a definitive "no telemetry channel
  available from this board" answer.
- **getCurrentSession() outlives isDriving() in DriveDetector**: `isDriving()`
  returns True only when `_driveState == DriveState.RUNNING`. Feeding a first
  zero-RPM value transitions RUNNING -> STOPPING immediately, flipping
  isDriving() to False. But the session stays alive — drive_end fires after
  `driveEndDurationSeconds` of wall-clock accumulates in STOPPING. Loops
  that need to wait for drive-end should check
  `detector.getCurrentSession() is not None`, not `detector.isDriving()`.
  Hit this writing tests/pi/simulator/test_scenario_arm.py.
- **scenario_builtins.py AND scenarios/*.json are the same truth, twice**:
  JSON files are loaded at runtime; python factory functions are used by
  tests and tooling. Drift between the two silently lets one representation
  fall out of date. Pattern: any test that exercises a JSON scenario should
  also load the factory and assert `len(json.phases) == len(factory.phases)`.
- **Full-cycle simulator idles at 800 rpm during park phase — doesn't
  trigger drive_end naturally**: the `full_cycle` scenario's last two phases
  (arrival + park) keep RPM at 800 which is well above the default
  `driveEndRpmThreshold=100`. Tests / demos that need drive_end emitted
  must explicitly `simulator.stopEngine()` (sets RPM=0) after the scenario
  completes, then keep feeding the detector for `driveEndDurationSeconds`.
- **Acceptance-grep self-reference trap**: when a story's acceptance is
  `grep -r 'old_pattern' … (no hits)`, you CANNOT leave the old pattern
  even in a "for historical context" comment ("legacy /home/pi/obd2 path
  removed"). The grep doesn't read prose — it only matches the literal.
  Rephrase the comment without the stale literal value. Hit this during
  US-179 service-file rewrite.
- **systemd venv ≠ install path**: the Eclipse project's venv convention
  is a dedicated home-dir venv (`~/obd2-venv` on Pi, `~/obd2-server-venv`
  on server) NOT `<install-path>/.venv`. `install-service.sh` must expose
  `--venv PATH` independently of `--path PATH`, otherwise post-install
  fails with "venv not found" when the two diverge.
- **journald > on-disk log files for systemd**: prefer default
  `StandardOutput`/`StandardError` (journal) over `append:/…/service.log`
  directives. Eliminates three failure surfaces (append-file creation in
  install-script, permission drift, rotation policy) and gives operators
  `journalctl -u <svc> -f` as a single source of truth.
- **Bash test grep `--` end-of-options guard**: when grep-asserting on a
  string that starts with `--` (like a CLI flag), use `grep -qF -- "$needle"`.
  Without `--`, grep treats `--init`/`--restart`/etc. as its own options and
  errors with "unknown option". Hit this writing tests/deploy/test_deploy_pi.sh:
  asserting "--help mentions --init" failed not because the help was missing
  the flag but because `grep -qF "--init"` parsed `--init` as a grep option.
- **Dry-run skips prerequisite checks, not just side effects**: a `--dry-run`
  mode that aborts because rsync isn't installed locally defeats its own
  purpose ("preview what WOULD happen"). Pattern: gate `require_rsync` and
  `require_ssh` behind `if ! $DRY_RUN`. The smoke test then runs offline on
  a workstation that doesn't have either tool — proving the dry-run preview
  is genuinely safe to run anywhere.
- **tar-over-ssh as a zero-install rsync fallback**: vanilla Windows git-bash
  ships without rsync. Pattern for deploy scripts that need rsync-like
  semantics on any machine: detect with `command -v rsync` and fall back to
  `tar -cz --exclude=... -f - . | ssh host 'cd … && find -mindepth 1 ... -exec rm -rf {} + && tar -xzf -'`.
  Trade-off vs rsync: no byte-level incremental (every file re-transfers),
  but tar preserves mtimes on extract, so content+mtime idempotency still
  holds. Remember to `find ! -name 'data' ! -name 'exports' ...` to preserve
  top-level runtime-state dirs the way rsync's `--exclude` does.
- **Session-flake vs durable harness gates**: if the Claude Code harness
  denies a Bash permission (e.g. `Bash(ssh:*)`) and prior sessions documented
  the same denial, probe once BEFORE giving up. Sessions 30/31/32 each hit
  an SSH denial on Sprint 10 Pi-Crawl stories and filed SPRINT_BLOCKED notes;
  Session 33 probed SSH first and it worked. One quick probe is cheap;
  assuming a prior blocker is permanent and exiting with SPRINT_BLOCKED
  costs a whole session. Cost asymmetry favors probing.
- **Scope-doNotTouch vs AC-requires: go closest-in-scope equivalent**:
  when a story's scope says e.g. `doNotTouch: deploy/` but an AC requires
  `systemctl start ...`, the scope wins. Don't broaden. Instead validate
  with the closest equivalent path (`kill -TERM` against a direct-invoke
  `python --simulate` process) and file a blocker with concrete options.
  The invariants (graceful teardown, no data loss, reverse component order,
  exit 0) are provable without invoking the literal AC phrasing. Hit this
  writing US-181 — systemctl was blocked by a pre-existing I-014 shadow
  bug in a service file I couldn't touch, so the direct-invoke proof
  carried the story.
- **DEBUG-level skip logs hide silent-degradation bugs**: if a module-level
  `try/except ImportError` sets an `X_AVAILABLE` flag and the decision is
  only logged at `logger.debug("X not available, skipping")`, the failure
  is invisible under normal INFO logging — the feature stays dead in
  production. Either promote to `logger.warning` OR log the exception
  type/message so operators see what the try/except caught. Hit this
  validating US-181 — HARDWARE_AVAILABLE was False under main.py load
  even though every dependency imports clean in isolation, and we only
  caught it by running `--verbose`. Tracked in TD-015.
- **Pytest wrapper around bash scripts**: when the thing under test is a
  shell script and the canonical test is also a shell script (per spec),
  add a thin tests/deploy/test_deploy_pi.py that invokes the .sh via
  `subprocess.run(['bash', str(SMOKE_TEST)], capture_output=True, ...)`.
  This makes the bash test discoverable by `pytest tests/` so it runs on
  every fast-suite run, while keeping the .sh as the source of truth for
  the assertions. Important: timeout must accommodate slow filesystems
  (NAS-mounted Z: takes ~35s to spawn 10 sub-bashes; 90s is safe headroom).
- **Drive-report section layering**: `formatDriveReport` uses keyword-only
  AI args (`analysis`, `recommendations`, `baselineCount`,
  `baselineEstablishedAt`) and short-circuits every new section behind a
  single `if analysis is not None` gate at the top.  Regression-invariant
  "drive with no AI data renders identically to before" becomes a
  structural property of the function, not just a test assertion — no
  other code path can accidentally emit the new sections.
- **Latest-completed-only semantics for CLI status surfaces**: when a
  table logs every attempt (AnalysisHistory: in_progress/completed/failed),
  the CLI should show the *latest completed* row and silently ignore
  failed/in_progress rows.  An empty 'AI Analysis' block is worse than
  no block — the CIO cares about "what did the AI actually say", not
  "how many times did we try".


- **Async → sync analytics bridge**: the analytics engine is sync (`Session`).
  From an async route, wrap it as
  `await session.run_sync(lambda s: doWork(s, ...))`. Mirrors the sync.py
  upsert-core pattern.
- **Service-layer exception vocabulary**: translate transport exceptions
  (`OllamaUnreachableError`, `OllamaHttpError` in ai/analyzer_ollama.py) to
  service-level equivalents (`OllamaUnreachable`, `OllamaHttpFailure` in
  services/analysis.py) before they reach the router. Keeps the API layer
  mapping one-to-one with HTTP status codes.
- **Prompt content loaded as files, not inlined**: system_message.txt /
  user_message.jinja are Spool-owned; Ralph loads via
  `Path(__file__).resolve().parent / "prompts" / ...` so Spool can edit
  without a code change.
- **Robust LLM JSON parsing**: try `json.loads()` first, fall back to
  `re.search(r"\[.*\]", raw, re.DOTALL)` for fenced or prose-wrapped output.
  Drop malformed items rather than failing the whole analysis.
- **Background asyncio task tracking**: `asyncio.create_task()` returns a
  strong reference that the event loop will GC if nobody holds it — known
  gotcha. Pattern: keep a module-level `set[asyncio.Task]`, add each task,
  register `task.add_done_callback(set.discard)` so the set auto-prunes on
  completion. Solves the GC issue AND gives tests a drain surface
  (`await asyncio.gather(*list(tasks), return_exceptions=True)`).
- **Blocking HTTP from async without httpx**: when a module already uses
  urllib sync for its core Ollama calls, keep it consistent — wrap urllib in
  `await loop.run_in_executor(None, _doBlockingCall)` rather than mixing in
  httpx. Keeps dependency surface small and transport style uniform.
- **Two-display-systems trap on Pi**: `src/pi/display/` (DisplayManager +
  headless/minimal/developer drivers — Adafruit SPI or stdout, NO pygame)
  is a distinct subsystem from `src/pi/hardware/status_display.py`
  (pygame + OSOYOO HDMI 480x320, battery/power/OBD status). They share
  zero code and are instantiated from different places in lifecycle.py.
  A story that says "pygame HDMI validation" is about the hardware
  module, not the display drivers. Check which one a story is actually
  about before writing tests. Hit this on US-178.
- **Silent ImportError disables whole hardware subsystem**: see TD-014.
  `src/pi/obd/orchestrator/lifecycle.py:39` uses `from src.pi.hardware.*`
  but `main.py` puts `src/` on sys.path so the right form is
  `from pi.hardware.*`. The `src.pi.*` form raises ImportError which is
  caught (HARDWARE_AVAILABLE=False), so HardwareManager is silently
  skipped at runtime on the Pi. Pattern to watch for: any `try: from
  src.*` block in a repo that uses `sys.path.insert(0, str(srcDir))`.
- **Pygame on a headless Pi over SSH**: `SDL_VIDEODRIVER=dummy` works
  (proves install), `kmsdrm` and `fbcon` both fail with "not available"
  because SSH sessions don't own a console seat. To render to HDMI you
  need a logged-in console session, a properly-configured systemd
  service with seat/logind, or an X/Wayland session. Put this in a
  story BEFORE writing "verify pygame via SSH" in acceptance criteria.
- **Scope-boundary stop-condition**: when a story's `filesToTouch` is
  narrow but its acceptance transitively requires code in `doNotTouch`
  territory, STOP and file an inbox note. Even a one-line fix across
  the boundary is worth a ~5-min inbox note instead of silent scope
  creep. Marcus (PM) pays the sprint-planning cost of surprise scope
  expansions. Hit this on US-178 (the TD-014 fix would have taken 60
  seconds but lived in `src/pi/obd/` — US-180's charter, not US-178's).


## 2026-04-19 — US-199 (Rex / Agent 1) — Sprint 14 Pi Harden Session 65 (PASSED)

Task: Spool Data v2 Story 1 — add 6 new Mode 01 PIDs + ELM_VOLTAGE
      adapter command to the Pi collector poll set with connection-open
      support probe, per-PID decoders, per-parameter_name registry, and
