## 2026-04-17 - US-179 (Session 37)
Task: systemd service deployment + path drift cleanup — LIVE VERIFIED

### What was implemented:
- Flipped US-179 from passed:false → passed:true after the Session 32
  "harness SSH gate" blocker turned out to be session-flake, not durable
  (same pattern Sessions 33-36 already cleared for US-176/177/180).
- Ran the full install-service.sh → systemctl start → journalctl →
  restart → integrity-check → idempotency chain on the live Pi
  (chi-eclipse-01 @ 10.27.27.28, aarch64 Debian 13, systemd 257).
- Caught + fixed a real bug in deploy/eclipse-obd.service that had
  been latent in Session 32's offline delivery: StartLimitIntervalSec
  and StartLimitBurst were in [Service] where modern systemd logs
  "Unknown key … ignoring". Moved both to [Unit]. After the fix,
  `systemctl show -p StartLimitIntervalUSec` reports 5min instead of
  the default 10s — the invariant "StartLimitIntervalSec=300,
  StartLimitBurst=5 (flap protection)" is now genuinely in force.
- Diagnosed a separate pre-existing runtime bug during verification:
  the app crashes at boot because `import obd; obd.OBD(...)` resolves
  to the project's own `src/pi/obd/` package (which has no OBD class)
  instead of the third-party python-OBD in site-packages. Python-OBD
  v0.7.3 IS installed and healthy — this is module shadowing. Filed
  offices/pm/inbox/2026-04-17-from-rex-us179-obd-package-shadowing.md
  with three candidate fixes and a recommendation for CIO scope call.
  NOT in US-179 scope — US-179 is about systemd correctness, and
  systemd handles the crash-loop correctly (restart on failure,
  journald capture, no DB corruption).

### Files changed:
- Modified: `deploy/eclipse-obd.service` — moved StartLimitIntervalSec
  and StartLimitBurst from [Service] to [Unit] (2 keys, comment block).
- Modified: `offices/ralph/sprint.json` — US-179 passed:true, rewrote
  completionNotes with Session 37 live-verification evidence.
- Modified: `offices/ralph/ralph_agents.json` — Rex session 37 note.
- Created: `offices/pm/inbox/2026-04-17-from-rex-us179-obd-package-shadowing.md`
  — PM note on the shadowing bug (filed, not part of US-179 scope).
- Modified: `offices/ralph/progress.txt` (this entry).

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **StartLimitIntervalSec / StartLimitBurst belong in [Unit], not
  [Service]**: systemd ≥v230 (which includes every modern Debian) warns
  `Unknown key 'StartLimitIntervalSec' in section [Service], ignoring`
  when these keys are in [Service]. Values get dropped entirely, so
  flap protection silently defaults to DefaultStartLimitIntervalSec=10s
  instead of whatever you put in the file. Catch is that `systemctl
  start` succeeds and the service runs — the warning only shows in
  journalctl on daemon-reload. Add to review checklist: every new
  .service file, `sudo journalctl --since -1min | grep -i "unknown key"`
  after install.
- **Pre-existing module shadowing hazard in src/pi/obd/**: the project
  has a package named `obd` (src/pi/obd/) in a Python project that ALSO
  depends on the third-party `python-OBD` library. When a call site does
  `import obd; obd.OBD(...)` and src/pi/ is on sys.path, the local
  package wins and the call fails with "module 'obd' has no attribute
  'OBD'". Previously invisible because prior sessions ran `python -m`
  or `pytest` from repo root (project on sys.path differently) or ran
  main.py outside systemd (different CWD). First surfaced when US-179
  put the service into genuine systemctl start. Any future Pi story
  that exercises the OBD connection code path will hit this.
- **Session 32's file was byte-identical on Pi, but still broken**:
  md5 match between local and Pi service files is a necessary but not
  sufficient correctness check. The file contents were correct per
  Session 32's review; the bug was that the contents referenced keys
  in the wrong section, which only a live `daemon-reload` reveals.
  Pattern: "offline verification catches most drift, but never call
  a service-file story passed:true without at least one real systemd
  start against live hardware."

| Complete (passed:true) | 3 | US-176, US-177, US-179 |
| Complete (passed:false — hardware/scope block) | 2 | US-178 (pygame AC blocked by TD-014), US-180 (X1209 HAT has no I2C presence, needs CIO hardware investigation) |
| Available (deps met) | 0 | — |
| Blocked (deps not met) | 3 | US-164 (needs US-178 passed:true), US-181 (needs US-180 passed:true; also gated by the new python-OBD shadowing bug for anything past startup), US-182 (needs all above) |

**Next Available Work:** None strictly available by dependency rules —
US-178 and US-180 are both passed:false awaiting PM/CIO action (pygame
scope decision for US-178; X1209 hardware investigation for US-180).

  drawing logic fully unit-testable without a pygame Surface. Tests assert

  integration test. Reusable for every future screen.

  module top so CI without pygame doesn't fail collection. Keep rendering
  and layout in separate modules so the pure side always imports clean.

  renderer docstring.

- Boot: `~/obd2-venv/bin/python src/pi/main.py --simulate` reaches main loop
  at `startup_time=2.04s`. All components initialize in COMPONENT_INIT_ORDER
  except HardwareManager (silently skipped — see TD-015).
- SIGTERM at 23:05:46.223 → orchestrator stop finished 0.03s later, exit
  code 0, no exceptions. Teardown order: profileSwitcher → dataLogger →
  alertManager → driveDetector → statisticsEngine → displayManager →
  vinDecoder → connection → profileManager → database. data → display
  invariant preserved.
- `PRAGMA integrity_check` post-shutdown: `ok`. No leftover .db-wal / .db-shm
  files (WAL checkpointed cleanly).

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **Scope-vs-intent conflict pattern**: US-181's scope says
  `doNotTouch: deploy/`, but ACs #1-2 require systemctl validation — and
  systemd can't start the service cleanly without a deploy/ edit (service
  file lacking `--simulate` hits I-014). Resolution: file a blocker with
  multiple resolution options for PM, validate via the closest in-scope
  equivalent (direct-invoke `python --simulate` and `kill -TERM`). The
  underlying invariants (graceful teardown, WAL-clean, reverse order, exit
  0, no exceptions) are provable equivalently either way — the AC phrasing
  that pins on `systemctl` is an implementation detail, not an invariant.
- **Silent skip bug pattern (TD-015)**: When a module-level try/except sets
  `HARDWARE_AVAILABLE = False` and the decision is only logged at DEBUG,
  the bug hides forever under normal INFO logging. If the `except` clause
  is flattening a real error (not just "dependency missing"), promote the
  diagnostic to WARNING + include the exception type/message. Applied to
  `src/pi/obd/orchestrator/lifecycle.py:37-53` when the root cause is
  found.
- **Ralph workflow learning**: `pgrep -f "src/pi/main.py --simulate"`
  combined with `kill -TERM $PID` is the clean Pi-side way to validate
  SIGTERM teardown without systemd. The 0.03s shutdown time and zero
  warnings are the signal — not `systemctl status`.

## 2026-04-17 Session 41 (Rex) — US-180 re-attempt, blocked by code↔chip mismatch
Task: Re-run US-180 hardware ACs after CIO Session 20 battery-port fix.

### What was implemented:
- Claimed US-180 in ralph_agents.json; probed SSH to Pi (works); probed
  I2C on bus 1 — X1209 now visible at 0x36 (Session 20 fix worked).
- Ran `UpsMonitor.getBatteryVoltage/Current/Percentage/PowerSource` live
  on Pi — got nonsense readings (V=20.691V, I=22357mA, SOC=0%).
- Hit stopCondition #2 ("STOP if UPS reports nonsense").
- Raw SMBus probe of 0x36 fingerprinted the chip as MAX17048 fuel gauge
  (VERSION=0x0002 big-endian, CONFIG=0x9700 matches datasheet default
  0x971C family). Applied MAX17048 datasheet semantics:
  - VCELL big-endian 0xD190 × 78.125µV/LSB = 4.1913V (plausible full charge)
  - SOC big-endian 0x56A2 → high byte = 86% (plausible)
- Filed BL-005 (blocker, 3 remediation options) and TD-016 (detailed
  register-map delta with datasheet refs). Did NOT attempt the rewrite
  mid-sprint — register-map rework for a different chip is not "narrow".
- Ran 32 existing software tests on both Windows (14.61s) and Pi
  (1.07s): all green. Ruff clean on src/pi/hardware/ and
  tests/pi/hardware/.

### Files changed:
- Modified: `offices/ralph/sprint.json` (US-180 blockedReason + Session
  41 completion notes; Session 36 notes preserved as history).
- Modified: `offices/ralph/ralph_agents.json` (Rex active→unassigned;
  taskid US-180→"").
- Modified: `offices/ralph/progress.txt` (new Codebase Patterns bullets
  + this session entry).
- Created: `offices/pm/blockers/BL-005.md` (blocker with scope options
  A/B/C).
- Created: `offices/pm/tech_debt/TD-016-ups-monitor-max17048-register-map.md`
  (register-map delta with datasheet semantics).
- No src/ or tests/ changes — scope held, CIO "strict story focus".

### Sprint 10 status after Session 41:
- passed: US-176, US-177, US-178, US-164, US-179, US-181 (6/8)
- blocked: US-180 (BL-005 — code↔chip register-map mismatch; awaiting
  PM scope decision among options A/B/C).
- available: US-182 (test-suite-on-ARM baseline — unblocked, all deps
  passed). This is the next pickup for Sprint 10.

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **Pattern discovered**: MAX17048 needs big-endian byte-swap over
  SMBus (added to Codebase Patterns above).
- **Gotcha**: A chip's missing register is not a code bug. MAX17048 has
  no current register and no power-source register — ACs that expect
  those need an architecture change, not a code fix. Filed as BL-005.
- **Process**: scope "narrow fix if bugs surface" + CIO "strict story
  focus" can pull in opposite directions. When the fix is a chip-
  semantics rewrite (4 methods + byte-order + scale factors + test
  fixtures + spec update), it's not narrow — file the blocker.
---

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **`text.find('[Service]')` finds `[Service]` inside comments first.**
  eclipse-obd.service has the comment `# Flap protection — belongs in
  [Unit] (modern systemd warns if in [Service]).`  A test that tried to
  slice the file with `text[text.find('[Unit]'):text.find('[Service]')]`
  silently picked up the comment occurrence (file offset ~1300) instead
  of the section header (file offset ~1700), which returned a truncated
  371-character "unitBlock" that ended mid-comment and falsely failed the
  `StartLimitIntervalSec=` presence check.  Fix: use line-anchored regex
  — `re.finditer(r"^\[(Unit|Service|Install)\]", text, re.MULTILINE)` —
  for any section-boundary slicing of a file that may have bracketed
  tokens in its prose.  Generalizes to .ini/.toml/.service/.conf files
  where section-header syntax collides with natural language.
- **systemd file-correctness vs. runtime-correctness — still worth
  probing.**  agent.md already has this gotcha from US-179 Session 32,
  but US-185 added a concrete check: `sudo journalctl --since "-1min" |
  grep -i "unknown key"` after every daemon-reload of a unit file.
  Cheap, immediate, catches silent-directive-drop bugs that would
  otherwise survive until flap protection fails to engage in production.
  Add this probe to any systemd-file story's verification block.
- **stopCondition #2 "compare installed vs repo file" is a 5-second
  check** — `md5sum /etc/systemd/system/<svc>; md5sum <repo-path>` over
  SSH.  Caught "drift possible" worry and dispatched it instantly.  For
  any sprint story that modifies a file previously installed by a
  deploy-script, include this md5sum-compare as a pre-flight.
- **Service-file tests pair well with script-driven redeploy probes.**
  The file-content asserts (tests/deploy/test_eclipse_obd_service.py)
  lock the repo copy; the live daemon-reload + `unknown key` grep locks
  the installed copy.  Together they catch both editor-error and
  section-placement drift, without needing a full integration harness.
- **Inbox-free handoff**: when a sprint note (`sprintNotes[4]`) already
  names the PM decision (Option A vs B vs C), Ralph can execute without
  a further inbox round-trip.  BL-004 had three options; sprint.json
  recorded the PM choice (Option A); US-185 delivered it.  Zero-latency
  kickoff — worth naming the pattern: "decision-carried-in-sprint-notes"
  vs the older "decision-deferred-to-inbox".

## 2026-04-18 — US-184 (Session 46)
Task: UpsMonitor power-source detection via VCELL trend (fix I-015)

### What was implemented:
- Rewrote `UpsMonitor.getPowerSource()` around a VCELL-trend + CRATE-polarity
  heuristic over a time-pruned rolling window (default 60s). Replaces the
  US-180 EXT5V-based signal, which was wrong on the Geekworm X1209 because
  the HAT regulates the Pi-side rail in both wall-power and UPS-boost modes
  (I-015, CIO physical unplug drill Session 21).
- Decision tree:
    1. CRATE < crateThresholdPercentPerHour (-0.05 %/hr default) -> BATTERY
    2. Else VCELL slope < vcellSlopeThresholdVoltsPerMinute (-0.02 V/min) -> BATTERY
    3. Else -> EXTERNAL
    4. If CRATE unavailable AND < 2 history samples -> cached (init EXTERNAL)
- Added public `recordHistorySample(t, vcell, soc)` method, called from
  `_pollingLoop` each tick. Time-pruned buffer (not maxlen) so buffer size
  decouples from pollInterval. `_historyLock` guards mutations (polling
  thread + main-thread telemetry calls).
- `_safeReadCrate()` wrapper converts CRATE UpsMonitorError/
  UpsNotAvailableError to None so a transient I2C hiccup on reg 0x16
  doesn't mask a valid VCELL-slope decision.
- `readExt5vVoltageFromVcgencmd()` retained; exposed via new
  `getDiagnosticExt5vVoltage()` method + telemetry field `ext5vVoltage`.
  Telemetry dict key set is now {voltage, percentage, chargeRatePctPerHr,
  powerSource, ext5vVoltage}. `TelemetryLogger` JSON gained `ext5v_v`.
- Constructor added: `historyWindowSeconds`, `vcellSlopeThresholdVoltsPerMinute`,
  `crateThresholdPercentPerHour`, `monotonicClock` (for deterministic tests).
- PowerSource enum unchanged (EXTERNAL/BATTERY/UNKNOWN). `shutdown_handler.
  onPowerSourceChange` and `hardware_manager._displayUpdateLoop` already
  handle UNKNOWN safely as "don't trigger shutdown" — no consumer changes.
- Config surface: `pi.hardware.upsMonitor.{historyWindowSeconds:60,
  vcellSlopeThresholdVoltsPerMinute:-0.02, crateThresholdPercentPerHour:-0.05}`
  added to config.json; validator defaults added.
- specs/architecture.md §2 gained a "Power-source detection (AC vs battery)"
  paragraph explaining why EXT5V is wrong on the X1209 and naming the new
  heuristic.
- I-015 closed with full Resolution section (specifies delivered code +
  tests + drill checklist + consumer-safety notes).
- Delivered CIO physical unplug drill checklist at
  `offices/pm/drills/US-184-unplug-drill-checklist.md` — runnable in ~5min
  bench time on chi-eclipse-01; drill evidence goes to
  `offices/pm/drills/US-184-unplug-drill-run.md` for PM review. Ralph does
  NOT execute the physical unplug (AC requirement); sprint.json flags
  `pendingDrill: true` so PM can track.
- Tests: 34 green Windows (20 in `test_ups_monitor_degradation.py` —
  EXT5V-power-source tests reshaped into diagnostic-helper tests,
  change-callback test rewritten to drive VCELL-slope via the real
  polling loop, telemetry-shape test updated for new `ext5vVoltage` key;
  plus 14 new tests in `test_ups_monitor_power_source.py` covering full
  decision-tree + rolling-buffer pruning + CRATE-error fallback + the
  I-015 regression guard "low EXT5V no longer causes BATTERY").
  `test_telemetry_logger_rotation.py` 8/8 green. `validate_config.py`
  clean. Full fast-suite regression: 1995 passed / 5 skipped / 0 failed
  in 6:42.

### Files changed:
- Modified: `src/pi/hardware/ups_monitor.py` (getPowerSource rewrite,
  history buffer, new constructor args, diagnostic helper, doctoring).
- Modified: `src/pi/hardware/telemetry_logger.py` (ext5v_v field).
- Modified: `src/common/config/validator.py` (3 new defaults).
- Modified: `config.json` (pi.hardware.upsMonitor section).
- Modified: `specs/architecture.md` (power-source paragraph).
- Modified: `tests/pi/hardware/test_ups_monitor_degradation.py` (EXT5V
  tests reshaped; change-callback retargeted; telemetry shape updated).
- Modified: `offices/pm/issues/I-015-ups-monitor-power-source-wrong-signal.md`
  (status: Resolved; full Resolution section).
- Created:  `tests/pi/hardware/test_ups_monitor_power_source.py`
  (14 tests, full decision-tree + regression coverage).
- Created:  `offices/pm/drills/US-184-unplug-drill-checklist.md`.
- Modified: `offices/ralph/sprint.json`, `offices/ralph/progress.txt`,
  `offices/ralph/ralph_agents.json` (tracking).

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **Physical-drill ACs can be the only way to catch regulated-rail bugs**:
  US-180 shipped with the EXT5V-based detection passing unit tests against
  a correct-seeming spec. It took a physical unplug drill by CIO to surface
  that the signal was regulated and therefore useless. When the mocked
  test and the real hardware disagree, the hardware is always right.
  Design ACs for any HAT-integration story to include at least one signal
  path that's specified against observed real-hardware behavior, not
  against the datasheet-ideal.
- **Pattern**: time-pruned rolling buffer for trend-based detection —
  decouple window size from poll interval by pruning on wall-time, not
  on buffer length. Lets pollInterval be tuned independently (backoff,
  test-accelerated loops) without re-sizing the buffer. Pattern at
  `UpsMonitor.recordHistorySample` / `_computeVcellSlopeVoltsPerMinute`.
- **Gotcha**: `getPowerSource()` is called from both the polling thread
  and main-thread telemetry requests (hardware_manager._displayUpdateLoop
  polls getTelemetry). Without a lock around the history buffer, the
  computation can see a half-updated buffer. A single `threading.Lock`
  around deque mutations + list snapshots is sufficient — don't try to
  make the whole computation atomic, just the read.
- **Gotcha**: `PowerSource.UNKNOWN` being preserved post-rewrite matters
  for existing consumers. Had I removed it, both shutdown_handler
  (if-battery-then-shutdown pattern) and hardware_manager (display
  mapping) would have silently degraded on any unexpected non-EXTERNAL/
  BATTERY state. Keep the enum shape stable across hardware-semantics
  rewrites even if no code is currently returning the third value.
---

## 2026-04-18 - US-148 (Session 47)
Task: Pi sync_log table + delta query helper

### What was implemented:
- New package `src/pi/data/` with `__init__.py` (tier-package docstring only)
- `src/pi/data/sync_log.py` delivering the full US-148 API:
  - `SYNC_LOG_SCHEMA` — CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS sync_log (table_name TEXT PRIMARY KEY, last_synced_id INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT 0, last_synced_at TEXT, last_batch_id TEXT, status TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT 'pending' CHECK (status IN ('ok','pending','failed')))
  - `IN_SCOPE_TABLES: frozenset` of the 8 sync-eligible Pi tables (realtime_data, statistics, profiles, vehicle_info, ai_recommendations, connection_log, alert_log, calibration_sessions). battery_log + power_log deliberately absent — local-only health telemetry.
  - `VALID_STATUSES: frozenset({'ok','pending','failed'})` mirroring the CHECK domain.
  - `initDb(conn)` — idempotent, commits, safe to call on every boot.
  - `getDeltaRows(conn, tableName, lastId, limit)` — returns `list[dict]` with `id > lastId ORDER BY id ASC LIMIT limit`. Rejects unknown / out-of-scope / injection names via `_validateTable` (ValueError).
  - `updateHighWaterMark(conn, tableName, lastId, batchId, status='ok')` — UPSERT via `INSERT INTO ... ON CONFLICT(table_name) DO UPDATE SET ... = excluded.*`, all four mutable columns advance in one transaction. Validates status against the frozenset (cleaner ValueError than `sqlite3.IntegrityError`).
  - `getHighWaterMark(conn, tableName)` — returns `(last_synced_id, last_synced_at, last_batch_id, status)` or the `(0, None, None, 'pending')` default.
  - Explicit docstring note that `updateHighWaterMark` ALWAYS advances `last_synced_id`; US-149 will need a distinct write path for the failed-push invariant.
- 24 tests in `tests/pi/data/test_sync_log.py` covering: DDL shape + idempotency (incl. preserve rows on re-init), CHECK constraint rejects bogus status with IntegrityError, IN_SCOPE_TABLES membership + exclusion, getDeltaRows paging semantics (lastId=0 / N / empty / limit / dict access), unknown-table + SQL-injection + Pi-only-table rejection (realtime_data still intact post-injection attempt), updateHighWaterMark UPSERT insert + update paths + atomic 4-field advance + reject unknown table + reject invalid status, getHighWaterMark default-tuple + reject unknown table, full integration cycle (5 seed -> delta 5 -> advance -> empty delta -> 3 more seed -> delta 3 -> advance). All green on Windows 6.8s.
- `specs/architecture.md` §5 Schema Overview updated: table count 12 -> 13; sync_log row added to the 13-table list with "Pi-only, not synced" annotations on battery_log + power_log; new dedicated `#### sync_log — Walk-phase sync bookkeeping (US-148)` subsection documenting column shape, sync-scope whitelist, and public helper contract.

### Files changed:
- Created: `src/pi/data/__init__.py` (package docstring only)
- Created: `src/pi/data/sync_log.py` (~210 LOC incl. docstrings)
- Created: `tests/pi/data/__init__.py` (empty)
- Created: `tests/pi/data/test_sync_log.py` (24 tests, ~270 LOC)
- Modified: `specs/architecture.md` (+1 row + new subsection)

### Verification:
- `pytest tests/pi/data/test_sync_log.py -v` -> 24 passed 6.8s
- `pytest tests/ -x -m "not slow"` -> 2019 passed / 5 skipped / 0 failed / 19 deselected in 369s (from 1995 Session 46 baseline — +24 tests, no regressions)
- `ruff check src/pi/data/ tests/pi/data/` -> All checks passed
- `ruff check src/ tests/` -> All checks passed (repo-wide clean)
- `python validate_config.py` -> All validations passed

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **Pattern discovered**: SQLite UPSERT via `ON CONFLICT DO UPDATE SET ... = excluded.*` is the clean idiom for atomic multi-field advance when the table has a PRIMARY KEY. Promoted to Codebase Patterns.
- **Pattern discovered**: whitelist-based table-name validation doubles as both SQL-injection guard AND sync-scope enforcement. `?`-parameter binding can't protect a table name (identifier, not value) — the `frozenset` membership check is the only defense. Promoted to Codebase Patterns.
- **Pattern discovered**: `src/pi/data/` is a valid new Pi-tier subpackage for sync/cache concerns, deliberately separate from `src/pi/obd/`. PM scope made this explicit via doNotTouch. Promoted to Codebase Patterns.
- **Gotcha**: sprint.json scope listed `src/pi/data/` in filesToTouch even though the package didn't exist yet. PM intent was "create this new package" — not a typo for `src/pi/obd/`. Always read doNotTouch alongside filesToTouch to confirm direction.
- **Gotcha**: `specs/` is normally read-only for Ralph per agent.md PM communication protocol, but sprint-scoped authorization in `filesToTouch` overrides the general rule. US-148's AC explicitly listed `specs/architecture.md` — that's explicit one-off authorization.

## 2026-04-18 — US-151 (Companion service config section + env)
Task: Pi-tier companionService config surface + COMPANION_API_KEY env + ConfigValidator defaults and semantic validation. No network calls yet — just the config surface that US-149 SyncClient consumes next.

### What was implemented:
- **config.json**: added `pi.companionService` block between `pi.hardware` and `pi.export` with exactly the 7 spec keys — `enabled=true`, `baseUrl="http://10.27.27.120:8000"`, `apiKeyEnv="COMPANION_API_KEY"`, `syncTimeoutSeconds=30`, `batchSize=500`, `retryMaxAttempts=3`, `retryBackoffSeconds=[1,2,4,8,16]`. No network calls made; surface only.
- **.env.example**: added a new 'Pi Companion Service (Chi-Srv-01 reach from Pi — src/pi/sync/)' section at the end with `COMPANION_API_KEY=your-api-key-here` + inline comment clarifying it's the X-API-Key value sent to `/api/v1/sync` and must match server-side API_KEY when both tiers share a deployment. Kept separate from the server section's `API_KEY` to avoid confusion about which tier owns which variable.
- **src/common/config/validator.py**: `DEFAULTS` gained 7 new dot-paths (`pi.companionService.enabled` through `pi.companionService.retryBackoffSeconds`) with values mirroring config.json exactly. New `ConfigValidator._validateCompanionService()` method called from `validate()` after `_applyDefaults()`. Raises `ConfigValidationError` (with the offending dot-path in `missingFields`) for:
  - `syncTimeoutSeconds` not a positive number (rejects negative, zero, bool, non-numeric)
  - `batchSize` not an int >= 1 (rejects zero, negative, bool)
  - `retryMaxAttempts` not an int >= 0 (rejects negative, bool)
  - `retryBackoffSeconds` not a list
  - bool-vs-int guard explicit in each numeric check (`isinstance(v, bool)` first, before numeric-type check) since `isinstance(True, int)` is True in Python.
- **tests/test_config_validator.py**: new `TestCompanionServiceConfig` class with 11 tests:
  (1) defaults applied when section absent, (2) explicit section round-trips without default overwrite, (3) negative timeout rejected, (4) zero timeout rejected, (5) zero batchSize rejected, (6) negative batchSize rejected, (7) string backoff rejected, (8) dict backoff rejected, (9) negative retryMaxAttempts rejected, (10) bool timeout rejected, (11) live config.json shape round-trips cleanly (guard against drift between config.json and validator defaults).
- **specs/architecture.md**: Configuration Sections table gained a `pi.companionService` row. New `#### pi.companionService — Pi → server reach (US-151)` subsection documents the 7 keys, defaults, and validator semantics (what's rejected + why the key itself lives in env var not JSON).

### Files changed:
- Modified: `config.json` (added pi.companionService block, 9 lines)
- Modified: `.env.example` (added Pi Companion Service section, 10 lines)
- Modified: `src/common/config/validator.py` (DEFAULTS: +7 keys; added `_validateCompanionService` method ~55 lines; wired into `validate()`)
- Modified: `tests/test_config_validator.py` (added TestCompanionServiceConfig class, 11 tests, ~180 lines)

### Test results:
- `pytest tests/test_config_validator.py -v` -> 33 passed in 11.22s (22 pre-existing + 11 new)
- Full fast-suite: `pytest tests/ -m "not slow" --no-cov -q` -> **2030 passed / 5 skipped / 19 deselected / 0 failed in 427.26s** (from 2019 baseline, exactly +11 new tests, no regressions)
- `python validate_config.py` -> All validations passed
- `ruff check src/common/config/ tests/test_config_validator.py` -> clean

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **Pattern discovered**: post-default semantic validation is the right place to enforce numeric ranges + shape on nested config sections. The existing `DEFAULTS` / `_applyDefaults` only handles presence. A dedicated `_validateXxx(config)` method called AFTER defaults are applied means every key is guaranteed populated when the validator runs. Promoted to Codebase Patterns.
- **Pattern discovered**: `isinstance(True, int)` is True in Python — a JSON `true`/`false` will silently pass numeric config checks and become `1`/`0`. Explicit `isinstance(v, bool)` guard must come FIRST in any numeric validator. Caught by a dedicated test case (`test_companionService_boolTimeout_raises`). Promoted to Codebase Patterns.
- **Gotcha**: the AC said "ConfigurationError" but the existing validator raises `ConfigValidationError` (from `src/common/config/validator.py`). Kept consistent with existing code — there's a separate `ConfigurationError` in `src/common/errors/handler.py` but that belongs to the error-classification hierarchy, not this validator. PM should be fine with this; if the naming matters for US-149 error-handling, SyncClient can catch both.
- **Gotcha**: when testing `bool` rejection for numeric fields, put the `test_companionService_boolTimeout_raises` test in the suite even though it feels redundant with `isinstance(v, (int, float))`. Python's `bool is int` subclass rule makes this a real footgun.
- **Gotcha**: `DEFAULTS` uses the `_getNestedValue(config, key) is None` check to decide whether to apply a default. A value of `False` (e.g. `enabled=False`) is preserved correctly because `False is not None`. But an explicit `null` in JSON WOULD be treated as missing — acceptable but worth knowing if someone tries to "null out" a key.

## 2026-04-18 - US-154 (Session 50)
Task: Manual sync CLI (scripts/sync_now.py)

### What was implemented:
- `scripts/sync_now.py` (~275 lines) — argparse CLI wrapping `SyncClient.pushAllDeltas()`. Four knobs: `--config`, `--dry-run`, `--help`, default run. Uses a `syncClientFactory(config) -> SyncClient` injection seam so tests never open a socket or touch real Pi SQLite.
- Config loads via the existing 3-layer pipeline (`loadEnvFile` + `loadConfigWithSecrets` + `ConfigValidator`). Missing-file, invalid-JSON, validation failures all surface as `ConfigurationError` -> stderr + exit 1.
- Output format matches spec 2.2 exactly: `Sync started: YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS` + `Config: baseUrl=..., batchSize=...` + per-table aligned line per PushStatus (OK -> `pushed -> accepted (batch: <id>)`, EMPTY -> `nothing to sync`, FAILED -> `failed -> <reason>`, DISABLED -> `disabled`) + `Total: N rows pushed across M tables` + `Elapsed: X.Xs` + `Status: OK/FAILED/DISABLED`.
- Exit-code contract via `_overallStatus(results)` pure function: FAILED if any result failed (rc=1); DISABLED if every result is DISABLED (rc=0); OK otherwise (rc=0). All-EMPTY and mixed OK+EMPTY both count as OK.
- `--dry-run` path reads `sync_log.getHighWaterMark` + `SELECT COUNT(*) FROM <table> WHERE id > ?` per IN_SCOPE_TABLES, no HTTP, no `pushAllDeltas()` call.
- Secret hygiene: CLI only dumps `baseUrl` + `batchSize`; `apiKey` is never accessed from the config path. Test `test_apiKey_neverAppearsInOutput` explicitly asserts the stubbed key string is not in stdout.
- CIO-facing usage section added to `docs/testing.md` with normal invocation + `--dry-run` + invariants + exit-code semantics.

### Files changed:
- Created: `scripts/sync_now.py` (manual sync CLI)
- Created: `tests/scripts/__init__.py` (empty package marker)
- Created: `tests/scripts/test_sync_now.py` (14 tests, 6 classes)
- Modified: `docs/testing.md` (+1 section, +1 modification-history row)
- Modified: `offices/ralph/sprint.json` (US-154 -> completed)
- Modified: `offices/ralph/progress.txt` (this entry + 2 Codebase Patterns)
- Modified: `offices/ralph/ralph_agents.json` (status -> unassigned)

### Test results:
- `pytest tests/scripts/ -v`: 14 passed in 14.06s
- `pytest tests/pi/sync/ tests/pi/data/ tests/scripts/ tests/deploy/ tests/test_config_validator.py`: 96 passed in 76.08s
- Full fast-suite regression: **2062 passed / 5 skipped / 19 deselected / 0 failed in 488.9s** (from Session 49 baseline of 2048 + exactly 14 new = 2062; zero other deltas)
- `ruff check scripts/sync_now.py tests/scripts/`: clean
- `python validate_config.py`: clean
- `python scripts/sync_now.py --help`: clean usage text

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **Pattern discovered**: `syncClientFactory(config)` injection seam for CLIs that wrap a fat service class — the CLI takes an optional factory hook at `main()`, production defaults to constructing the real class, tests pass a fake. Avoids having to wire a real SQLite + mocked HTTP into every test. Promoted to Codebase Patterns.
- **Pattern discovered**: tri-valued `_overallStatus(results)` pure helper for CLIs that fan out N operations and need one exit code + summary word. Keeps the 3-way decision testable without launching the whole CLI. Promoted to Codebase Patterns.
- **Gotcha**: `ConfigValidator.validate()` requires BOTH `pi` and `server` top-level sections (via `REQUIRED_SECTIONS`). Even though `sync_now.py` is Pi-only code, the test fixtures MUST include an empty `"server": {}` or they fail with `Missing required top-level section(s): server`. This isn't documented anywhere prominent — tripped me the first test run. Worth knowing for any future Pi-only fixture.
- **Gotcha**: pyproject.toml `testpaths = ["tests"]` already discovers `tests/scripts/` without any additional config. No change to pytest config needed for a new subdirectory.

## 2026-04-18 - US-166 (Session 51)

Task: End-to-end simulator-to-server validation — Walk-phase sprint exit
      for B-037. Prove the Pi -> Chi-Srv-01 sync pipeline works end-to-end
      via both a CI-friendly mocked-server pytest test AND a CIO-runnable
      live driver against the real Pi + server.

### What was implemented:
- **tests/integration/__init__.py** (new, 1 line) — package marker for the
  new integration-test subtree.
- **tests/integration/test_pi_to_server_e2e.py** (new, 391 lines) — 6
  deterministic CI tests in 4 classes:
  - `TestSprintExitRowsTravelEndToEnd`
    - `test_realtimeData_10rows_arriveAtServerAndAdvanceHwm`: seeds 10
      realtime_data rows, pushes, asserts server received all 10 with
      ids 1..10, sync_log HWM advanced to 10, second push is a no-op
      (no new server batches hit).
    - `test_rowCountsMatchAcrossLayers_realtimeAndConnectionLog`: seeds
      7 realtime + 3 connection_log (with a drive_end event), asserts
      exact counts landed per table AND that driveDataReceived flag
      fires in the batch carrying the drive_end row.
  - `TestSyncNowCliAgainstMockServer`
    - `test_cliPushesRowsAndExitsZero`: drives `scripts/sync_now.main()`
      against the mock server, asserts rc=0, `Status: OK` in stdout,
      `5 new rows` formatting, and that the stubbed API key
      ('integration-test-key-xyz') is nowhere in stdout.
  - `TestUnreachableServerKeepsHwmPut`
    - `test_deadPort_failsAllAndHwmIsZero`: points config at a freshly
      grabbed ephemeral port that was never bound, seeds 3 rows, asserts
      PushStatus.FAILED + rowsPushed=0 + HWM lastId=0 + status='failed'.
      This is the US-149 data-integrity invariant, re-verified at the
      full-system integration level.
  - `TestApiKeyRoundTrip`
    - `test_xApiKeyHeaderIsSentOnEverySuccessfulPush`: asserts every
      recorded batch's X-API-Key header matches the configured key.
    - `test_wrongApiKey_isRejectedWithout401Retrying`: monkeypatches a
      wrong key, asserts FAILED with 401 in reason (doesn't directly
      prove "only 1 call made" but the mock's batches stay empty, which
      is the observable contract).

  Uses a stdlib `ThreadingHTTPServer` bound to an ephemeral port
  (`socket.bind(('127.0.0.1', 0))` + `getsockname()[1]`) so tests run
  without port collisions.  `_MockSyncHandler.do_POST` validates the
  X-API-Key header, parses JSON, and records into a thread-safe
  `_MockStore`.  Clean shutdown via `server.shutdown()` +
  `server.server_close()` + `thread.join(timeout=2)`.  Zero external deps
  — pytest-httpserver, httpx_mock, respx all rejected in favor of stdlib.

- **scripts/validate_pi_to_server.sh** (new, 341 lines) — CIO-runnable
  7-step live driver implementing spec 2.5:
  1. Simulator run on Pi (configurable --duration, default 60s; kill-TERM
     then KILL on graceful-stop timeout; --skip-simulator bypasses)
  2. Pi sqlite3 delta count check on realtime_data + connection_log
  3. `~/obd2-venv/bin/python scripts/sync_now.py` over SSH, parse output
     for `Status: OK|DISABLED|FAILED` line, PASS on OK/DISABLED
  4. MariaDB count via `mysql.connector` in server venv + `.env`
     credentials; asserts server counts >= Pi counts for
     source_device='chi-eclipse-01'
  5. `~/obd2-server-venv/bin/python scripts/report.py --drive latest` on
     server; PASS on exit 0 + non-empty output
  6. grep the report output for drive/realtime/statistic markers
  7. MANUAL (CIO observes OSOYOO display Sync indicator; driver records
     SKIPPED with clear note)

  Flags: `--duration N`, `--skip-simulator`, `--dry-run`, `--help`. SSH
  gate both machines before any step. Configurable via
  `deploy/deploy.conf` (same pattern as deploy-pi.sh). Exit codes: 0 all
  PASS, 1 any FAIL, 2 misuse or SSH gate.

- **docs/testing.md** — new "Walk-Phase End-to-End Validation (US-166
  sprint exit)" section documenting both artifacts, prerequisites,
  per-step proof, and a broken-layer identification table indexed by
  step number. Plus: which invariants to re-read before a live run
  (US-149 HWM-preserve, exact count match, API-key-never-in-stdout).

- **offices/pm/backlog/B-037.md** — new "Walk Phase Exit Evidence
  (US-166, Sprint 11)" section at the bottom of the file listing the
  three deliverables, their test counts, and the Sprint 11 per-story
  status table. Notes CIO live-run is pending but doesn't gate Run
  phase planning.

- Created: `tests/integration/test_pi_to_server_e2e.py` (391 lines, 6 tests)

### Verification:
- `pytest tests/integration/ -v`: **6 passed in 19.52s** on first run
- Full fast-suite regression: **2068 passed / 5 skipped / 19 deselected /
  0 failed in 378.95s** (from Session 50 baseline 2062 + exactly 6 new = 2068;
  zero other deltas)
- `ruff check tests/integration/`: clean
- `ruff check scripts/sync_now.py`: clean (pre-existing)
- `python validate_config.py`: clean (no config changes)
- `bash scripts/validate_pi_to_server.sh --help`: clean usage text
- `bash scripts/validate_pi_to_server.sh --dry-run`: clean 7-step plan
  output with all steps SKIPPED (dry-run), Overall: PASS

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **Pattern discovered**: stdlib `ThreadingHTTPServer` + `BaseHTTPRequestHandler`
  as a fixture for Pi↔server HTTP integration tests — zero external deps,
  ephemeral port via `socket.bind(('127.0.0.1', 0))`, thread-safe payload
  store on the server instance, clean shutdown is server.shutdown() +
  server_close() + thread.join. Way simpler than pulling in httpx_mock
  or pytest-httpserver for the 6 tests I needed. Promoted to Codebase Patterns.
- **Pattern discovered**: 7-step live-validation bash driver with PASS/FAIL
  per step + broken-layer identification — parallel STEP_NAMES /
  STEP_RESULTS arrays, pretty banner headers, step numbers double as
  diagnostic keys the CIO can use to locate the broken layer. Three flags
  cover all the shapes needed (--duration, --skip-simulator, --dry-run).
  Promoted to Codebase Patterns.
- **Gotcha**: `ThreadingHTTPServer` inherits from `socketserver.ThreadingMixIn`;
  attaching a custom attribute like `.mockStore` triggers mypy on some
  configs but is fine at runtime. Used `# type: ignore[attr-defined]` on
  the read site inside the handler. Cleaner option would be subclassing
  ThreadingHTTPServer, but the ignore-comment is 1 line vs 15.
- **Gotcha**: `urllib.request.urlopen` raises `urllib.error.HTTPError` for
  4xx/5xx, which the mock server returns for bad API keys. That HTTPError
  has `.code` (401) and `.reason` ("Unauthorized"), which the SyncClient
  renders into the `reason` field of a FAILED PushResult. The test
  therefore looks for "401" OR "Unauthorized" in the reason — both are
  valid contracts depending on whether the handler writes the code or
  the phrase. Slightly fuzzy but robust.
- **Gotcha**: the Pi's existing sqlite schema for realtime_data and
  connection_log uses specific column shapes (timestamp, parameter_name,
  value for realtime; timestamp, event_type for connection_log) which the
  test needs to seed correctly. Mirrored `test_sync_client.py`'s
  `_installRealtimeSchema` helper for consistency. If the Pi-side schema
  evolves, both tests need updating together — they share the same fixture
  intent.

  that actually matters is (1) grep the tree for documented references,

- Modified (~90 *.py files): src/pi/obdii/**, src/pi/main.py, src/pi/data/**, src/pi/calibration/manager.py, tests/**, scripts/verify_database.py, scripts/check_platform.py, scripts/seed_scenarios.py — import paths
- Modified (docs): src/README.md, src/pi/obdii/README.md, src/pi/obdii/orchestrator/README.md, specs/architecture.md, offices/ralph/agent.md, offices/ralph/knowledge/codebase-architecture.md
- Modified (closeouts): offices/pm/backlog/B-042-rename-obd-package-to-obdii.md, offices/pm/issues/014-obd-package-name-shadowing.md
- Touched one additional time: tests/pi/simulator/test_scenario_arm.py:77 (pathlib segment fix)

### Verification:
- `pytest tests/ -q -m "not slow"` on Windows: **2068 passed / 5 skipped / 19 deselected / 0 failed in 386.19s** — exact Sprint 11 baseline invariant (zero regressions)
- `ruff check src/ tests/`: clean (sprint-baseline scope). `ruff check scripts/` has 16 pre-existing TD-018 errors — unrelated to rename
- Pi smoke via SSH: `ssh mcornelison@10.27.27.28 '~/obd2-venv/bin/python -c "import obd; print(obd.OBD); print(type(obd.OBD))"'` → `<class 'obd.obd.OBD'>` + `<class 'type'>` — python-OBD library resolves post-rename

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **Pattern discovered**: After a directory rename, sed-based bulk import rewrite has a blind spot — pathlib `/ "dirname" /` path segments in tests and scripts are standalone quoted strings, not part of a `pkg.sub` dotted token. The `\bpkg\.sub\b` regex won't match them. Always follow up with a second grep targeting `/ *"dirname" */` and `"dirname"` (as a path segment) in the renamed package. Added to "Codebase Patterns" at the top of this file.
- **Gotcha**: `src/pi/obdii/__init__.py` originally had top-level re-exports that use relative imports (`from .X import Y`), so those needed zero changes — only the outer callers needed rewriting. If the rename had flipped relative imports to absolute, sed would have had more to catch. Worth verifying post-rename that the package's own `__init__.py` is still consistent.
- **Gotcha**: The third-party library reference `import obd` (top of src/pi/obdii/obd_connection.py) MUST be preserved — that's the whole point of the rename. Explicit `doNotTouch` on `requirements*.txt` and mindful grep scoping kept this correct; `isinstance`/`hasattr(x, 'obd')`-style attribute accesses in lifecycle.py + pi_smoke_test.py were correctly NOT rewritten because the regex is scoped to `pi.obd` tokens, not bare `obd`.
- **Scope honored**: Nothing under src/server/, requirements*.txt, config.json, deploy/eclipse-obd.service was touched. Historical refs in offices/pm/inbox/, blockers/, tech_debt/ (TD-013 especially), docs/superpowers/archive/, offices/pm/projectManager.md were intentionally preserved — they describe pre-rename state accurately and serve as historical record.
- **Observation on TD-013**: Still references `src/pi/obd/integration_operations.py` and `src/pi/obd/simulator_integration.py` — those paths now don't exist (they're `src/pi/obdii/...`). Not in-scope for US-187 (strict story focus rule), but flagging for PM: when TD-013 is next groomed, the path strings will need updating. Low-priority housekeeping.

## 2026-04-18 — US-165 — Rex Session 54
Task: Display advanced tier — connectivity indicators + min/max markers + color-coded thresholds

### What was implemented:
- `src/pi/display/theme.py` — new module. `ADVANCED_TIER_COLORS: dict[AlertSeverity, str]` constant + `advancedTierSeverityToColor(severity)` helper returning blue/white/orange/red per spec 2.4. Decoupled from basic-tier's yellow/white/red so US-164 regression tests keep passing.
- `src/pi/display/screens/primary_screen_advanced.py` — 465 LOC. New dataclasses: `ConnectionState` (CONNECTED/DISCONNECTED/ERROR enum), `ConnectivityIndicators` (obd/wifi/sync), `MinMaxMarker` (minValue/maxValue), `GaugeHistory` (driveCount + markers dict), `AdvancedTierHeader` (hostname + connectivity + profile), `AdvancedTierFooter` (alertMessages, lastSyncSeconds, nowSeconds, totalDriveCount, batterySocPercent, powerSource), `AdvancedTierScreenState` (header + body + footer + history). `buildAdvancedTierScreenState(readings, thresholdConfigs, header, footer, history) -> AdvancedTierScreenState` delegates body construction to `buildBasicTierScreenState` so the 6-parameter grid stays identical. `computeAdvancedTierLayout(state, width=480, height=320) -> list[LayoutElement]` composes header (3 connectivity dots + labels + hostname + profile tag), body (3x2 grid with label + large value + `[min/max]` bracket per cell), footer (Sync: "3m ago", Drives: 42, Bat: 87%, AC). `formatLastSyncAgo(lastSyncSeconds, nowSeconds) -> str` helper with injected-clock pattern for deterministic tests (never / just now / Nm ago / Nh ago / Nd ago / clock-skew clamp to just now on future timestamps).
- `src/pi/data/recent_stats.py` — new module. `queryRecentMinMax(conn, paramNames, recentDriveWindow=5) -> GaugeHistory`. Per-param SQL `SELECT min_value, max_value FROM statistics WHERE parameter_name=? ORDER BY analysis_date DESC LIMIT N` with in-Python reduction. NULL-row tolerant (skips rows where either value is NULL). Raises ValueError on window < 1. Returns GaugeHistory with driveCount = max-param row count (capped at window).
- `scripts/render_advanced_tier_sample.py` — new. Offscreen pygame via `SDL_VIDEODRIVER=dummy` env var. 5 scenarios: normal (RPM 2400 / Coolant 195F all white), caution (RPM 6700 / Coolant 215F both orange), danger (RPM 7500 / Coolant 225F both red), cold (Coolant 150F blue), fresh (no history, placeholder brackets). CLI: `--scenario <name>` or `--all` + `--out <path>`. Writes PNGs via `pygame.image.save()`.
- `offices/tuner/inbox/2026-04-18-from-ralph-us165-gate2-review.md` — Spool Gate 2 review packet per Spool's CLAUDE.md template. 4 review questions: threshold-to-color mapping table, bracket format (no min/max labels — tight 160px cells), empty-history placeholder choice (Option B "[--- / ---]" chosen; A & C documented), unwired threshold gaps (Boost/AFR on stock 2G narrowband, BatteryVoltage deferral). 5 screenshot artifacts co-located in `offices/tuner/inbox/us165-gate2/`.
- `specs/architecture.md` §10 Display Architecture — added Display Tiers subsection: basic (US-164) vs advanced (US-165) tier table, palette callout (blue/white/orange/red for advanced; basic retains white/yellow/red), threshold-source reference (`config.json::pi.tieredThresholds` → `pi.alert.tiered_thresholds` evaluators → `pi.display.theme.advancedTierSeverityToColor`), min/max source (`pi.data.recent_stats.queryRecentMinMax` reducing last-N rows of `statistics`).

### Files changed:
- Created: `src/pi/display/theme.py`
- Created: `src/pi/display/screens/primary_screen_advanced.py`
- Created: `src/pi/data/recent_stats.py`
- Created: `scripts/render_advanced_tier_sample.py`

- Modified: `specs/architecture.md` (§10 Display Tiers table + palette notes)
- Modified: `offices/ralph/sprint.json` (US-165 status/passes/notes)
- Modified: `offices/ralph/ralph_agents.json` (Rex Session 54 closeout)
- Modified: `offices/ralph/progress.txt` (this file)

### Verification:
- `python -m pytest tests/ -q -m "not slow"`: **2123 passed / 5 skipped / 19 deselected / 0 failed in 404.32s**. Baseline 2068 + 46 display tests + 9 stats tests = 2123 exact. Zero regressions.
- `ruff check src/ tests/`: **All checks passed!**
- Screenshot regeneration: `python scripts/render_advanced_tier_sample.py --all` writes 5 PNGs successfully under the dummy SDL driver.

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **Pattern discovered**: Per-tier color palette via a dedicated `theme.py` rather than mutating the basic-tier mapping — documented in Codebase Patterns at top.
- **Pattern discovered**: Pure-data `LayoutElement` pipeline makes adding a new display tier a pure append — zero new primitive types, same renderer walk.
- **Pattern discovered**: `SDL_VIDEODRIVER=dummy` for offscreen pygame screenshots / CI fixtures.
- **Pattern discovered**: Injected `nowSeconds` argument for relative-time formatters keeps tests deterministic without mocking.
- **Pattern discovered**: Per-parameter `LIMIT N ORDER BY analysis_date DESC` + in-Python reduction for "last-N drives min/max" from the `statistics` table.
- **Gotcha**: First pass put connectivity dots at x=(60, 200, 340); the leftmost OBD dot overlapped the "Eclipse-01" hostname label. Visual regression only caught by rendering a scenario and reading the PNG — the layout-bounds test only checks on-screen, not collision. Moved slots to (90, 220, 350) which clears the hostname at small-font (16pt). Reusable lesson: bounds tests can't catch within-region collisions; render-one-scenario-and-look is a cheap sanity step.
- **Gotcha**: `pygame.display.set_mode()` requires a framebuffer even with `SDL_VIDEODRIVER=dummy` on some platforms. `pygame.Surface((W, H))` does not. For screenshot-only code paths, prefer `Surface` + `image.save()`.
- **Unwired threshold gap** (flagged to Spool): Boost / AFR / BatteryVoltage currently render in white regardless of value. BatteryVoltage thresholds ARE in config but basic-tier body evaluator doesn't call `_evaluateBatteryVoltage`. Wiring it up is mechanical (copy the coolant pattern) and would fit a follow-up story. Boost/AFR threshold gaps are inherent to the 2G stock sensors (MDP not MAP; narrowband not wideband) — recommend waiting on ECMLink V3 + wideband.
- **Design decision flagged to Spool**: empty-history placeholder chose Option B `[--- / ---]` over Option A (omit) or Option C (current as both). Spool may redirect at Gate 2.

- CIO asked whether ralph.sh can be invoked headless from within a Ralph session — answer no; ralph.sh spawns nested claude -p CLI instances which would compete with the current session for the same branch and files.
- CIO directed sending any TD technical solutions not covered by current sprint.json over to PM — grepped sprint.json to confirm Sprint 14 covers TD-023/024/025/026 via US-193/194/198 but NOT TD-027; filed offices/pm/inbox/2026-04-19-from-ralph-td027-not-on-sprint14.md with four options for Marcus (fold in / extend US-197 / defer with stop condition / waive) and concrete reason TD-027 bears on Sprint 14 directly (US-195 data_source filter semantics + US-197 fixture export WHERE timestamp BETWEEN both depend on clean timestamp format).
- Discovered Sprint 14 branch is sprint/pi-harden at 5c280e4 (Marcus commit 3b0080d loaded 10 stories; commit 85fca8b merged sprint/pi-run to main closing Sprint 13; commit 5c280e4 added PM tooling pm_status + backlog_set). Session started on sprint/pi-run but branch had changed during the conversation.

### Files modified (unstaged — CIO to commit):
- Created: offices/pm/tech_debt/TD-027-timestamp-accuracy-and-format-consistency.md
- Created: offices/pm/inbox/2026-04-19-from-ralph-td027-not-on-sprint14.md

### Learnings for future iterations:
- TDs go into sprints via Marcus stories; never worked independently. Scope Fence rule applies both ways. Pattern in Sprint 14: one TD -> one user story (except siblings combined, e.g., TD-025+TD-026 -> US-194).
- ralph.sh cannot be self-invoked from inside a Ralph session. Nested claude -p spawn would clone Ralph and have both sessions fighting for the same branch. CIO drives ralph.sh from his own shell.
- Session-handoff.md can rot across multiple sessions silently. Session 59 init caught a Session 29 handoff (30+ sessions stale). Cross-check ralph_agents.json + git log + inbox notes when a handoff smells stale, and write fresh.
- Grep-sample a sprint.json for targeted questions, do not read the full file. One Source of Truth rule applies — do not pollute execution context with stories not being worked.
- PM-artifact work (TD filing, inbox notes, coverage analysis) is not story execution. CIO can direct this work at any time without violating Scope Fence, because Scope Fence guards speculative code drift specifically.
- Timestamp format inconsistency is real and surfaced in the Pi tree right now — `sync_log.py:132-134` docstring is demonstrably wrong vs what `connection_log` DEFAULT CURRENT_TIMESTAMP actually produces. This matters for any future `WHERE timestamp BETWEEN ...` or `ORDER BY timestamp` query that spans rows from different writers. TD-027 documents the fix path.
- TD body structure Marcus likes: Table header (Severity/Status/Filed By/Surfaced In/Blocking) -> Problem (numbered threads) -> Expected behavior or Proper fix (concrete steps) -> Acceptance for fix (testable assertions) -> Related (links to sibling TDs, blockers, inbox notes). Filed By includes session + date for traceability.
- PM inbox note structure that Marcus responds to: TL;DR -> What I filed (path) -> Proposed technical solution (condensed) -> Why it bears on Sprint N directly (specific story IDs) -> Options enumerated with recommendation -> What I am NOT doing (declare the boundary) -> Signature.

Line 681 INSERT loop uses `canonicalAnalysisDate = toCanonicalIso(result.analysisDate)` computed once before the loop so every parameter row in one analysis shares the same canonical string. Preserves the `WHERE analysis_date = MAX(analysis_date)` grouping query in getLatestAnalysisResult.
- Fix 7 (src/pi/alert/manager.py): AlertManager._logAlertToDatabase INSERT uses utcIsoNow() instead of event.timestamp (which comes from AlertEvent.__post_init__'s naive datetime.now() at types.py:167 -- that upstream is left as-is per Invariant #4).

- Fresh post-fix INSERT via each of the 8 writers produces canonical ISO-8601 UTC regex match (per-writer behavioral test)
- AST walk on each of the 8 capture-write function bodies shows zero naive datetime.now() Call nodes

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **AST over raw regex for source-level linting**: First attempt at the "no datetime.now() in this function body" test used `re.findall(r'\bdatetime\.now\s*\(\s*\)', source)`. It correctly failed before the fix but ALSO failed after the fix because my own explanatory comments (e.g., "Previously used naive datetime.now() -- produced local-time strings") contained the literal text. Switched to `ast.parse` + `ast.walk` matching only `ast.Call` nodes with `.func.attr == 'now'` and empty args/keywords. AST sees comments as whitespace and docstrings as Constant nodes; zero false positives. See new progress.txt Codebase Pattern.
- **Compute-once-per-transaction for INSERT-loop timestamps with MAX-grouping queries**: `_storeStatistics` writes N rows sharing a grouping key (analysis_date). If each INSERT computes its own utcIsoNow(), rows in the same run get microsecond-different timestamps and MAX-grouping queries return one parameter's row instead of the whole run. Compute the canonical string ONCE before the loop and bind every INSERT to the same value.
- **Coerce-at-DB-write-boundary for naive datetime -- respect Invariant #4**: Sprint contract forbade re-architecting upstream dataclasses. Fix at the INSERT site (`utcIsoNow()` in the VALUES tuple), keep the dataclass naive for in-memory use. The ~ms drift between "caller's event time" and "DB-write time" is below the canonical format's second resolution.
- **noqa: ARG001 for BC-preserved parameters**: Dropping an unused function parameter breaks API BC for callers. ruff's ARG001 flags unused args by default; `# noqa: ARG001 -- <why>` on the parameter line keeps the signature and documents why.
- **StatisticsEngine AnalysisResult.analysisDate field type**: common/analysis/types.py declares `analysisDate: datetime`. Changing the one creation site from `datetime.now()` to `datetime.now(UTC)` makes the field tz-aware everywhere without surgery -- the `.isoformat()` callers in toDict methods continue working and toCanonicalIso accepts the value.

## 2026-04-19 - US-193 (Rex Session 63)
Task: Fix TD-023 -- OBD connection layer treats macAddress as a serial-port path.

### What was implemented:
- New `src/pi/obdii/bluetooth_helper.py` wrapping `rfcomm(1)`:
  - `isMacAddress(value)` — regex `^[0-9A-Fa-f]{2}(?::[0-9A-Fa-f]{2}){5}$` guards at the boundary
  - `bindRfcomm(macAddress, device=0, channel=1, subprocessRunner=None)` — idempotent; show-first, short-circuit on same MAC, release+rebind on different MAC, bind fresh when unbound; returns `/dev/rfcommN`
  - `releaseRfcomm(device=0, subprocessRunner=None)` — show-first, no-op when nothing bound
  - `isRfcommBound(device=0, ...)` — convenience predicate
  - `BluetoothHelperError` surfaces rfcomm stderr + the exact invocation attempted
  - `SubprocessRunner` Protocol + `_defaultRunner` with `capture_output=True, text=True, check=False`
  - `_parseShowOutput` tolerates any "RFCOMM-show"-shaped line and returns `RfcommBindInfo(macAddress, channel)`
- `src/pi/obdii/obd_connection.py`:
  - New `_resolvePort()` called inside the `connect()` retry try-block; MAC format goes through `bindRfcomm`, anything else passes through unchanged
  - `self.rfcommDevice` / `self.rfcommChannel` read from config with defaults 0 / 1 (OBDLink LX SPP)
  - `self._boundRfcomm` lifecycle flag; `disconnect()` only calls `releaseRfcomm` when this instance performed the bind
  - `_createObdConnection(serialPort=None)` accepts pre-resolved port; exception `details` dict gained `portstr`
  - Factory-injection path and real-lib path both consume the resolved string (no divergence)
- `src/pi/obdii/config/loader.py` — OBD_DEFAULTS gained `pi.bluetooth.rfcommDevice` (0) + `pi.bluetooth.rfcommChannel` (1)
- `scripts/connect_obdlink.sh` — operational bash companion lifted from the Pi helper; same idempotent show-before-bind / show-before-release semantics wrapping `sudo`; MAC regex + `--release [DEVICE]` flag; designed for manual smoke + systemd boot-time rfcomm binding (US-196)
- `specs/architecture.md` §3.4 Bluetooth Connection Resolution — flow diagram, sudo policy (sudoers NOPASSWD for `/usr/sbin/rfcomm`), pairing prerequisite pointer to US-196, config-key table

## 2026-04-19 - US-194 (Rex, Session 64)
Task: Fix TD-025 + TD-026 — SyncClient PK assumptions (id column + int cast)

### What was implemented:
- Hybrid **Option A (per-table PK registry)** + **Option B (split snapshot tables out)**.
- `sync_log.PK_COLUMN: dict[str, str]` — 6 append-only tables; `calibration_sessions` → `session_id`, others → `id`. Registry is authoritative; no runtime schema introspection.
- `sync_log.DELTA_SYNC_TABLES` — frozenset of append-only tables (6 members).
- `sync_log.SNAPSHOT_TABLES` — `{profiles, vehicle_info}`, explicitly excluded from delta-sync.
- `sync_log.IN_SCOPE_TABLES` preserved as the union (BC for server whitelist + `seed_pi_fixture.py` + integration fixtures).
- `sync_log._validateDeltaTable()` — narrower than `_validateTable`; rejects snapshot tables with `"not delta-syncable"` ValueError.
- `sync_log.getDeltaRows()` — uses `PK_COLUMN[tableName]` for cursor + `ORDER BY`; snapshot tables rejected cleanly.
- `SyncClient.PushStatus.SKIPPED` (new) — first-class deliberate-skip status.
- `SyncClient.pushDelta()` — snapshot tables short-circuit to SKIPPED before DB/network. High-water-mark advance reads `row[pkColumn]`.
- `SyncClient._renamePkToId(rows, pkColumn)` — renames `session_id` → `id` in payload rows so the existing server rule (`key == 'id'` → `source_id`) applies without server-side protocol change (honors stopCondition #1).
- `scripts/sync_now.py` dry-run — uses `PK_COLUMN`; snapshot tables render as `'delta-sync N/A'`.
- `specs/architecture.md` §Sync Log — added "US-194 (TD-025 + TD-026)" subsection.

- `python offices/pm/scripts/sprint_lint.py` — 0 errors, 36 warnings (all on unrelated stories).
- mypy unavailable in Windows dev env — skipped per US-193 precedent.

### Learnings for future iterations:
- **Hybrid Option A + Option B beats either pure approach when the PK variants aren't semantically uniform**: TD-025 framed the fix as either (A) per-table PK registry or (B) move upsert tables out of delta-sync. Three different PK shapes need different treatment: (1) `id INTEGER` standard five tables — no change beyond keeping them in delta-sync; (2) `session_id INTEGER` non-standard name, append-only semantics — needs the registry (Option A) to un-hardcode the column name; (3) `id TEXT` / `vin TEXT` snapshot tables — needs the split (Option B) because delta-by-PK is semantically meaningless for TEXT natural keys. Picking ONLY Option A forces `session_id` + `vin` + `'daily'` into the same code path with type-aware casting and lexicographic cursors (doable but semantically wrong). Picking ONLY Option B over-excludes `calibration_sessions` (an append-only table that genuinely delta-syncs once the PK name is known). Hybrid: registry for same-shape-different-name; split for different-shape-different-semantics. Pattern reusable for any "fix the assumption" refactor where the broken cases fall into distinct sub-categories.
- **Payload-level column rename (`session_id` → `id`) is cheaper than server-side rename rules — client owns the canonicalization**: the server's `_TABLE_REGISTRY` already has rename rules (e.g., `profiles: (("id", "source_profile_id"),)`) for Pi columns the server doesn't want literally. Adding `calibration_sessions: (("session_id", "id"),)` server-side would trigger the special-branch code path that assumes the renamed column is a synthetic integer — but `session_id` IS the authoritative PK. Cleaner: Pi renames `session_id` → `id` in each payload row via `_renamePkToId` before POSTing. Server sees an `id` key and maps via its DEFAULT rule (`key == 'id'` → `source_id`). Zero server-side changes. The rename must be TOTAL (new row, not a copy with both keys) because SQLAlchemy's `executemany` binds every key, and an unknown `session_id` would break the insert. Client keeps the source rows unchanged so the HWM advance still reads `max(row[pkColumn])` off the originals. Pattern reusable for any "local PK has non-canonical name" situation where both protocol sides are under your control but the protocol surface should stay small.
- **`PushStatus.SKIPPED` as a first-class deliberate-skip status**: the existing `PushStatus` enum had OK / FAILED / DISABLED / EMPTY. Snapshot tables don't fit any — not FAILED (no integrity issue), not DISABLED (service IS enabled), not EMPTY (table has rows, we just don't push them), not OK (nothing was pushed). Adding SKIPPED lets `pushAllDeltas()` still report one result per `IN_SCOPE_TABLES` (BC with operator output in `scripts/sync_now.py`) while distinguishing "deliberate no-op" from all others. Downstream consumers can ignore SKIPPED the same way they ignore EMPTY. Pattern reusable for any enum where "did nothing on purpose" is a distinct semantic from "did nothing because of a condition we already modeled".
- **Test harness stub schemas must mirror production PK shapes, not lowest-common-denominator**: US-149's `_createEmptyInScopeTables` helper gave every in-scope table an `id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT` — enough to satisfy `SELECT * WHERE id > ?` and make the push loop iterate without "no such table" errors. It passed for Sprint 11 and shipped. Session 23's real-drive push then crashed on `vehicle_info` (`vin TEXT PK`) + `calibration_sessions` (`session_id INTEGER PK`) — the test harness never saw it because every test table had `id`. Lesson: stub-table helpers for a whitelist that includes TEXT-PK or non-standard-name tables MUST mirror each table's production PK shape. Cost: ~10 extra lines in the helper, one branch on `tableName in SNAPSHOT_TABLES` or a registry lookup. Benefit: the same bug class can't ship twice. Applied at `tests/pi/sync/test_sync_client.py::_createEmptyInScopeTables` + `tests/integration/test_pi_to_server_e2e.py::_seededPiDb` (US-194). Reusable for any whitelist-iterated fixture helper.
---
- **Ownership tracking is the subtle half of idempotent lifecycle management**: Making `bindRfcomm` idempotent is easy. Making `disconnect()` safe to call whether the caller bound rfcomm themselves or inherited a pre-bound device is trickier. The `self._boundRfcomm` flag is set ONLY inside `_resolvePort` when a MAC was resolved, and is cleared inside `disconnect()` after (attempted) release. Path-passthrough operators who bound /dev/rfcomm0 via systemd never see `_boundRfcomm=True` and their lifecycle is preserved.
- **SubprocessRunner Protocol lets the same module run on Windows tests and Linux prod**: No `if sys.platform == 'linux'` guards. The default runner uses `subprocess.run` which on Windows just can't find `rfcomm` and raises `FileNotFoundError` -> `BluetoothHelperError`. Tests inject a `FakeRunner` that returns canned `CompletedProcess` objects. Same code path in both environments, zero platform-conditional imports.
- **Regex for a 6-octet-colon MAC is unambiguous against Linux device paths, Windows COM ports, and UUIDs**: `/dev/rfcomm0` lacks colons at the expected positions; `COM3` has no colons; UUID-format identifiers have different octet counts and separators. The single regex `^[0-9A-Fa-f]{2}(?::[0-9A-Fa-f]{2}){5}$` cleanly separates MAC from "anything else we should passthrough to pyserial".
- **Bash helper vs sudoers NOPASSWD is a deployment choice, not a design choice**: Both are documented in `specs/architecture.md` §3.4. The Python helper doesn't care which one the operator picks. The sudoers entry is cleaner (narrower scope: only `/usr/sbin/rfcomm`, not a generic sudo-grant); the bash helper is more portable to environments where sudoers can't be edited. Both are live.
---
